PLAN 1:

Summary Plan Description

TPMG Employees

Benefits effective January 1, 2017

(including amendments through December 31, 2017)

                  Retirement Plan for Physicians & Salaried Employees

                     of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc.
May 2022

          SUMMARY OF MATERIAL MODIFICATIONS

To: Participants and Beneficiaries of The Retirement Plan for Physicians and Salaried Employees of
         The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. ("Plan 1")

This is a summary of material modifications (SMM) to the retirement plan listed above. No action is
required. This SMM updates your Summary Plan Description (SPD) for this Plan and should be retained
with your SPD. Specifically, this SMM describes changes to the tax laws governing the timing of benefit
payments.

New Required Beginning Date for Required Minimum Distributions

When you stop working and if you are eligible, you can receive a distribution, or you may defer
payments no later than the date the Internal Revenue Service requires you to take a first withdrawal.
This is referred to as the Required Beginning Date (RBD) for Required Minimum Distributions (RMDs).
RMDs cannot be rolled over to an individual retirement account or other qualified retirement plan.

Previously, employees had to begin receiving RMDs from qualified retirement plans by April 1 of the
later of the calendar year following the year they reached age 70.5 or retired, which is the RBD. The
Setting Up Every Community for Retirement Enhancement Act (SECURE) increased the age from 70.5
to 72 for individuals who reached age 70.5 after December 31, 2019. The Plan was updated to reflect
this change. You must begin receiving RMDs from the Plan by April 1 of the later of the calendar year
following the year you reach age 72 or retire from TPMG.

If you have questions, please contact the National Human Resources Service Center at (877) 457-4772.
MD Benefits, The Permanente Medical Group, Inc.

Retirement Plan for Physicians and Salaried Employees of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc.
EIN/Plan Number: 94-2728480/011

                                                                                                                      Salaried Employees, Plan 1
November 2021
                                    SUMMARY OF MATERIAL MODIFICATIONS

To: Salaried Employee Participants and Beneficiaries in the following benefit plans:
          Retirement Plan for Physicians and Salaried Employees of The Permanente Medical Group,
             Inc. ("Plan 1")
          The Permanente Contribution Plan of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. ("Plan 2")

This is a summary of material modifications ("SMM") made to Plan 1 and Plan 2 (the "Plans"). The Plans
provide pension benefits and also fund retiree medical benefits for eligible employees and their
dependents. This document should be retained with your Summary Plan Descriptions.
This SMM clarifies the optical coverage available to employees and dependents who are eligible for
retiree medical benefits under the Plans.
Optical Coverage
Optical coverage is provided to all Salaried Employees who are eligible for retiree medical benefits
under the Plans and who choose to enroll in the Kaiser Foundation Health Plan medical plan. As
explained in the "How Retiree Medical Coverage Works" section of your SPD, you also have the option
to choose the Preferred Provider Option (PPO) medical plan, which does not include optical coverage.
If you have any questions, please contact the National Human Resources Service Center (NHRSC) at
877-457-4772.

Retirement Plan for Physicians and Salaried Employees of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc.
EIN/Plan Number: 94-2728480/011
The Permanente Contribution Plan of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc.
EIN/Plan Number: 94-2728480/040
Salaried Participants
February 2020

               SUMMARY OF MATERIAL MODIFICATION

To: Salaried Participants, Beneficiaries and Employees who are Participants or may become eligible for:

 Retirement Plan for Physicians and Salaried Employees of The Permanente Medical Group,
    Inc. ("Plan 1")

 The Permanente Contribution Plan of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. ("Plan 2")

This is a summary of material modifications made to Plan 1 and Plan 2. These plans also fund retiree medical
benefits. This document should be retained with your Summary Plan Descriptions.

No action is required by you.

Plan 1 ­ New Immediate Payment Option

Salaried Employees who are vested in Plan 1 may elect to commence benefit payments immediately
following termination of employment by electing the Immediate Retirement Income Option. This option
will be available beginning January 1, 2021 to all vested Salaried Employees (including those whose
termination date is before 2021). The current plan rules, which permit such distributions only to employees
who have earned 10 years of service or, reached age 65 or become disabled, will continue to apply until
January 1, 2021. Under the current plan rules, benefit payments that begin before age 65 are actuarially
reduced to reflect the earlier payment date based on the employee's age at the time payments begin. The
factors used to determine the amount of the reduction under the Immediate Payment Option are the same as
those used to determine Retirement Income under the current 10-Year Early Retirement Option. Please see
your Summary Plan Description for more information about how the amount of your Retirement Income is
determined.

Medicare Part B Premiums Reimbursement for Rehired Retirees
If you are a retiree eligible for Medicare Part B premiums reimbursement, they will be suspended if you are
rehired as an employee of TPMG (or another Medical Care Organization such as Kaiser Foundation Health
Plan).

Medicare premiums that are incurred during the period of reemployment are not eligible for reimbursement.

Medicare premiums reimbursement will resume when your TPMG employment ends if you are eligible for
retiree medical benefits under this Plan at that time.

This modification does not change other eligibility rules.

Optical Coverage
Effective January 1, 2020, optical coverage is provided to all Salaried Employees who are eligible for retiree
medical coverage. Previously, certain retirees hired before February 1, 1986, did not receive optical
coverage.

If you have any questions, please contact the National Human Resources Service Center at 877-457-4772.

The Permanente Contribution Plan of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc.

June 2019

                               SUMMARY OF MATERIAL MODIFICATION

To: Salaried Employees who are Participants in the following plans of The Permanente Medical
         Group, Inc. ("TPMG"):

          Retirement Plan for Physicians and Salaried Employees of The Permanente Medical Group,
             Inc. ("Plan 1")

          The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. Salary Deferral Plan ("Plan 3")

This is a summary of a material modifications that have been made to Plan 1 and Plan 3. This document
should be retained with your Summary Plan Descriptions ("SPD").

Payment Start Date for Employee's Surviving Spouse

Effective January 1, 2018, if an employee dies before receiving pension benefits from Plan 1 and the
employee's spouse is his or her sole beneficiary, the spouse can defer payment of benefits until the year
after the employee would have reached age 70.5. Previously, a spouse beneficiary could defer payment
of benefits only until the month in which the employee would have reached age 65.

2017 Wildfire Relief ­ Distribution and Recontribution

Employees who received a distribution from Plan 3 in connection with the October 2017 California
wildfires before December 31, 2018, have the option to repay all or part of that distribution to Plan 3
within three years. The employee may qualify for a tax deduction if the distribution is repaid in
accordance with IRS rules. Your tax advisor can tell you if you qualify for a tax deduction.

Updated Hardship Withdrawal Rules

Effective January 1, 2019, hardship withdrawals are available from Plan 3 without first taking a plan
loan, and contributions may continue uninterrupted following receipt of a hardship withdrawal.
Previously, IRS rules did not permit hardship withdrawals until all available Plan loans had been taken,
and required contributions to be suspended for six months after receipt of a hardship withdrawal.
Hardship withdrawals are limited to an employee's pre-tax and Roth contributions (including earnings)
and are only available if the employee has insufficient assets available to cover an immediate and heavy
financial need, as defined by Plan 3. Your SPD provides further information about hardship withdrawals,
including the types of expenses that constitute an immediate and heavy financial need.

If you have any questions, please contact the National Human Resources Service Center (NHRSC) at
877-457-4772.

MD Benefits, The Permanente Medical Group, Inc.

About this Summary

This document is the summary plan description ("SPD") for the Retirement Plan for
Physicians and Salaried Employees of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc., also known as
"Plan 1." As a SPD, this document is only a summary of the full plan provisions which are
in the official plan document. The terms of the official plan document govern if there are
differences between the summary and the official plan document.

While The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. ("TPMG") expects the plan to continue to be a
part of its members' benefit program, it reserves the right to amend, merge, modify, or
terminate the plan, in whole or in part, at any time. In addition, TPMG does not promise
that any benefits included in the plan will continue to be offered. TPMG reserves the right to
reduce, eliminate, and add or increase the amount of required or optional member and
beneficiary contributions for health and medical, at any time and for any reason.

Participation in the plan does not give you rights to any benefit except as expressly provided
in the plan. Also, participation in the plan does not:

 give you rights to continued employment by TPMG,

 in any way prohibit changes in the terms of your employment, and

 in any way limit TPMG's right to terminate your employment for any reason.

As required by IRS rules, if you are married and younger than age 35, you may not designate someone
other than your spouse to receive more than one-half of your plan benefit.

If you marry after designating a non-spouse beneficiary, your designation to your non-spouse
beneficiary will no longer be valid and the following will occur:

 If you have not yet retired, your designation will automatically be your new spouse.

 If you have already retired, you may designate your new spouse as your new beneficiary if you are
    receiving your benefit in the form of a fixed period certain and life annuity or installment
    payments. See "Fixed Period and Life Annuity" on page 19 and "Installment Payments" on page
    19 for details on these options.

 If you had already retired and elected a Joint Retirement Income Option/Joint and Last Survivor
    Annuity, your joint annuitant, including a former spouse, named at the time benefits commenced,
    will continue to receive the benefit payments after your death.

Service that Does Not Count as Credited Service

The following service does not count as hours of credited service:

 Service with any organization after you are no longer employed by TPMG, unless you are later re-
    employed as a salaried employee eligible to participate in the plan;

 Hours for which TPMG has been required to make non-elective contributions to an individual
    retirement account or defined contribution plan, pursuant to a collective bargaining agreement; and

 Service after a member becomes covered by a collective bargaining agreement that does not
    provide for participation in this plan.

Years of Credited Service

You earn a year of credited service for each calendar year after 1990 in which you have at least 2,000
hours of credited service.

In addition, credited service that was recognized before January 1, 1991 under the Salaried Retirement
Plan is recognized under Plan 1.

If you have less than 2,000 hours of credited service in a calendar year, you will receive credited
service for that year on a proportional basis.

You will receive proportional credit service, but only if you were scheduled to work at least one
half of the full-time work schedule of your department.

Retirement Plan 1 for Salaried Employees
Retirement Plan 1 for Salaried Employees

                                                         Vesting Service

Benefits at a Glance Being vested means that you have a non-forfeitable right to receive the benefits you have earned under

                                the plan. But if your employment ends before you are "vested," you lose the benefits you have earned.

Calculating the Normal RFoer dteitariels,mseee"RnettireBe eMendiecafl iBtenefits" on page 25.

Your normal retirement benefit is based on the following formula:

                                             The greater of

               1.5% of your HAC for each year of credited
                                                           service

                                                                Or

                     $17.50 for each year of credited service

                                                              Plus

             0.25 % of your HAC for each year of credited
                                service before January 1, 1968

                                                             Minus
Any amount payable to you under another retirement plan
sponsored by a MCO that uses the same credited service
to determine your benefit as is used under Plan 1.

Example of Calculating Normal Retirement Benefit

The example below shows how a benefit estimate is calculated Assumptions:

 You reach age 65 and retire on December 31, 2017,

 You have 25 years of credited service, and

 Your HAC on December 31, 2017 is $5,000.

     You end employment with TPMG and all MCOs at age 55 after 12 years of vesting service.

      Because you have 12 years of vesting service, eight years later, when you reach age 63, you will
         eligible for early retirement (63 + 12 years of vesting service equals 75).

Note: If you begin your benefit before age 65, your benefit will be actuarially reduced to reflect the
fact that your payments are beginning early and are expected to be paid for a longer period.

Deferring Payment Past Age 65

If you are no longer working for TPMG or MAPMG at age 65, you may defer commencement of
your vested benefit past age 65.

If you defer payment of your benefit beyond age 65 and you have stopped working for TPMG and
MAPMG, the full benefit will be actuarially increased as shown in the following table. The increase
reflects the delayed payment and the shorter period of time it is expected to be paid. If you continue
to work past age 65, this increase will not apply until you stop working, but you will continue to earn
benefits.

Benefits Effective January 1, 2017                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              15

Limits on Payment Periods For details, see "Retiree Medical Benefits" on page 25.

Under the 100% joint and last survivor annuity, fixed period and life annuity, and installment payment
options, you cannot elect a payment period that is greater than your life expectancy, or, if applicable,
the combined life expectancy of you and your beneficiary.

  Making Your Election Regarding Form of Payment

  You must elect your form of payment during the 90-day period before benefit payments are scheduled to
  begin. Any election regarding the time and form of payment must be made no earlier than 90 days before
  your benefits begin and in the form and manner designated by the plan administrator. You may revoke
  your election at any time BEFORE you start receiving benefits. You will not be allowed to revoke your
  election or change the payment form after you start receiving benefits. ONCE PAYMENTS BEGIN, YOU
  CANNOT CHANGE THE FORM OF PAYMENT.

Single Life Annuity

If you are not married, the normal form of payment is a single life annuity. If you elect a single life
annuity, you receive a monthly benefit payable for as long as you live. Upon your death there will be
no further payments to your spouse, estate, or beneficiary.

If you are married, you must have your spouse's notarized consent to elect a single life annuity.

If you die before benefits have been paid for the guaranteed period, the monthly pension benefit
payments will continue to your beneficiary until the end of the guaranteed period.

Naming a Beneficiary

If you elect a fixed period and life annuity, you will be required to name a beneficiary to receive the
remainder, if any, of the fixed period and life annuity remaining upon your death. If you are married, you must
provide the proper spousal consent documentation to elect this option.

Installment Payments

If you elect installment payments, you receive fixed monthly payments over a specified period you
choose when you retire, up to a maximum of 30 years or 360 months, subject to IRS rules.

After the specified period has ended, no further benefits will be paid.

If you die before the specified period ends, the monthly payments will continue to your beneficiary
for the remainder of the specified period.

Naming a Beneficiary

If you elect installment payments, you will be required to name a beneficiary to receive the remainder, if any,
of the installment payments remaining upon your death. If you are married, you must provide the proper
spousal consent documentation to elect this option.

 Demonstrates compliance with the requirement that benefit decisions follow the terms of the plan
    and be consistently applied to similarly situated claimants.

Appeal Process

The Administrative Committee or its designee will decide your appeal within a reasonable period of
time, but no later than 60 days (45 days if your claim is for disability benefits) after it receives your
appeal. However, the Administrative Committee (or designee) may need more time -- up to 120 days
(90 days if your claim is for disability benefits) after it receives your appeal -- to make a decision due
to special circumstances. If an extension of time is required because of special circumstances, you will
be given written notice of the extension before the expiration of the initial determination period. The
written extension notice will indicate the special circumstances requiring the extension and the date by
which the committee expects to render a decision.

The Administrative Committee (or designee) will consider all comments, documents, records, and
other information that you have submitted in reviewing your claim, regardless of whether that
information was considered in determining your initial claim. If your claim is for disability benefits, the
review must not defer to the original denial and must be decided by the Administrative Committee or
its designee.

Retirement Plan 1 for Salaried Employees
Retirement Plan 1 for Salaried Employees

                       If you do not receive notice within the time allowed, you should consider your claim denied. Decisions

                       by the Administrative Committee are final, binding, and conclusive on all concerned and shall be given

Before Your Pension Benefit Payments Begin

If you have a vested Plan 1 benefit and you die before you have submitted a valid signed benefit
election form and your retirement benefit payments have not begun, a pre-retirement death benefit is
payable to your beneficiary. If you are not vested when you die, no survivor's benefit is payable to
your beneficiary from the plan.

If you die before you qualify for normal retirement benefits, the pre-retirement death benefit is
actuarially equivalent to the greater of:

 The normal retirement pension benefit you had earned at the date of your death, or

 For a surviving spouse, if you were eligible for early retirement when you died, the survivor
    portion of the 662/3% joint and survivor annuity as if you had retired on the day before you died.

Your beneficiary may elect to receive the pre-retirement death benefit in the form of:

 a single life annuity,

 a single payment,

 a fixed period and life annuity, or

 installment payments.

The monthly pension benefit payable to your beneficiary after your death will depend on your
beneficiary's age and the form of payment elected by your beneficiary.

Additionally, the medical benefits provided by this plan for members and beneficiaries covered by
Medicare are intended only to supplement Medicare payments. All such medical benefits, and the cost
to TPMG of providing such benefits, are based on the Medicare benefits that existed on January 1,
1994. If, at any time, Medicare pays less of the medical benefits provided to members and
beneficiaries under this plan than the amount paid by Medicare on January 1, 1994, there is no
obligation on the part of TPMG to provide additional benefits or to incur additional costs.

Eligibility and Enrollment

This section describes the eligibility requirements for retiree medical benefits for you and your family.

If you are eligible for post-retirement medical benefits, you should contact the KPRC at 866-627-2826 or
http:/kp.mercerbenefitscentral.com to confirm your coverage.

Cost of Coverage

TPMG makes contributions for post-retirement medical benefits. The contributions are deposited in a
separate account under the plan where they are held by the plan trustee for the sole benefit of eligible plan
members, their spouses, and their qualified dependents.

Effect of Divorce or Legal Separation on Coverage

When there is a divorce or legal separation, your spouse is no longer eligible for coverage. Coverage
for your spouse will terminate at the end of the month in which KPRC is notified. You are required
to contact KPRC at 866-627-2826 and provide a copy of the court order for dissolution of marriage
or legal separation within 60 days of the date the divorce or legal separation became effective. Failure
to provide timely notification will jeopardize eligibility for continued coverage under COBRA to your
former spouse.

Coverage May End If You Are Re-employed

Any retiree medical benefits you are receiving from the plan will stop if you become eligible for
medical benefits for active employees after being rehired by TPMG or a MCO.

 If you are rehired by TPMG, you will again become eligible for benefits from the plan when your
    employment ends.

 If you are rehired by a MCO and you become eligible for medical benefits from that MCO's plan,
    you will no longer be entitled to benefits under this plan.

Other Rules and Regulations Post-Retirement Medical Benefits You, your spouse and your eligible children may be eligible for retiree medical benefits through Plan 1.

This section describes additional rules and regulations that may affect your Plan 1 benefits, as well as
your rights under laws such as the Employee Retirement Income Security Act of 1974 (as amended),
known as "ERISA."

PBGC-Insured Benefits

Benefits under this plan are insured by the Pension Benefit Guaranty Corporation ("PBGC"), a
federal insurance agency. If the plan ends without enough money to pay all benefits, the PBGC will
step in to pay pension benefits. Some people will receive all of the pension benefits they would have
received under the plan, but some people may lose certain benefits. The PBGC guarantee generally
covers:

 normal and early retirement benefits;

 disability if you become disabled before the plan terminates; and

 certain benefits for your survivors.

The PBGC guarantee generally does not cover:

 benefits greater than the maximum guaranteed amount set by law;

 some or all of the benefit increases and new benefits based on plan provisions that have been in
    place for fewer than five years when the plan ends;

 benefits that are not vested because you have not worked long enough;

 benefits for which you have not met all the requirements when the plan ends;

                       Under ERISA, there are steps you can take to enforce the above rights. For instance, if you request a

                       materials were not sent because of reasons beyond the control of the plan administrator.

If You Leave Before Age 65  If you are vested and leave TPMG and all MCOs before age 65 with less than 10 years of vesting service and
                            you are not eligible for early or disability retirement, you are eligible to begin receiving your benefits as a
                            deferred vested retirement benefit on the first day of the month following the month in which you reach age 65.

                            You may begin receiving your benefits before age 65, if you become eligible for early or disability retirement
                            before then. You become eligible for early retirement when the sum of your age and your years of service
                            equals 75 or more, or when you reach age 55, if you had at least 15 years of service at termination.

                            For details, see "Deferred Vested Benefit" on page 15. See also "When Benefits Can Be Paid" for other rules.

                            For details, see "If You Are Re-employed" on page 23.

                            receive benefits.

                            For details, see "Benefits If You Die" on page 23.

Post-Retirement Medical Benefits You, your spouse and your eligible children may be eligible for retiree medical benefits through Plan 1.

                            For details, see "Retiree Medical Benefits" on page 25.

Summary Plan Description

The Permanente Contribution Plan

May 2022

          SUMMARY OF MATERIAL MODIFICATIONS

To: Participants and Beneficiaries of the following retirement plans:

 The Permanente Contribution Plan of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. ("Plan 2")
 The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. Salary Deferral Plan ("Plan 3")

This is a summary of material modifications (SMM) to the retirement plans listed above (Plans). No
action is required. This SMM updates your Summary Plan Descriptions (SPDs) for these Plans and
should be retained with your SPDs. Specifically, this SMM describes changes to the tax laws governing
the timing of benefit payments to you and your beneficiaries and the availability of plan loans.

New Required Beginning Date for Required Minimum Distributions

When you stop working and if you are eligible, you can receive a distribution, or you may defer
payments no later than the date the Internal Revenue Service requires you to take a first withdrawal.
This is referred to as the Required Beginning Date (RBD) for Required Minimum Distributions (RMDs).
RMDs cannot be rolled over to an individual retirement account or other qualified retirement plan.

Previously, employees had to begin receiving RMDs from qualified retirement plans by April 1 of the
later of the calendar year following the year they reached age 70.5 or retired, which is the RBD. The
Setting Up Every Community for Retirement Enhancement Act (SECURE) increased the age from 70.5
to 72 for individuals who reached age 70.5 after December 31, 2019. The Plans have been updated to
reflect this change. You must begin receiving RMDs from the Plans by April 1 of the later of the calendar
year following the year you reach age 72 or retire from TPMG.

Required Minimum Distributions for Beneficiaries

Previously, the general distributions rules to beneficiaries of deceased participants required that full
account balance distributions take place no later than December 31 of the calendar year in which the
participant died; by December 31 of the calendar year in which the deceased participant would have
reached age 70; or by the end of the year of the 5th year after the participant died. The timing rules
varied depending on the beneficiary.

The SECURE Act changed the timing rules for distributions to most beneficiaries for participants who
die after December 31, 2019. In general, under the SECURE Act, most beneficiary account balances
must be fully distributed by the end of the 10th year after the year the participant dies. Special rules
apply to certain types of beneficiaries, including spouses, minor children, trusts and others. Plan 2 and
Plan 3 have been updated to reflect changes made by the SECURE Act.

No action is required. As always, you may designate a Plan beneficiary or change your Plan beneficiary
at any time. Contact MD Benefits at (510) 625-6600 if you wish to designate a beneficiary or review or
change your current Plan beneficiary designations.

If you have questions about how the SECURE Act changes may affect the timing of payments to your
beneficiaries, you should speak with a qualified estate planner or financial planner.
Temporary Changes Relating to COVID-19
Plan 2 and Plan 3 have been updated to reflect legislation that temporarily changed the rules relating
to retirement plan loans and distributions.
Temporary Increase to Maximum Plan Loan Limit
Plan 2 and Plan 3 allow you to borrow from your account balances and repay the funds with interest
by requesting up to two loans not to exceed the $50,000 combined plan loan maximum. Under the
Coronavirus Aid, Relief and Economic Security Act (CARES Act), the maximum plan loan temporarily
increased from $50,000 to $100,000 to eligible plan participants who experienced a financial loss due
to COVID-19, certified the need for financial assistance, and requested a Plan loan from May 1, 2020,
through September 23, 2020.
Temporary Option to Suspend Plan Loan Payments
Under the CARES Act, eligible plan participants who experienced a financial loss due to COVID-19 that
affected their ability to make timely loan payments and certified the need for financial assistance, had
the option to suspend the loan payments from April 20, 2020, through December 31, 2020.
Temporary Option to Suspend Minimum Required Distributions
Due to the significant market volatility caused by the COVID-19 pandemic, the CARES Act allowed
participants in Plan 2 and Plan 3 to elect to take Required Minimum Distributions (RMDs) or to
temporarily suspend the distributions for the 2020 plan year.
Temporary Option to Receive Early Plan Distribution due to Financial Loss (Plan 3 Only)
Under the CARES Act, eligible Plan 3 participants who experienced a financial loss due to the COVID-19
pandemic and certified the need for financial assistance, had the option to receive a distribution of up
to $100,000 during 2020 and to recontribute the full distribution to the plan over a three-year period.

If you have questions, please contact the National Human Resources Service Center at (877) 457-4772.

This is a summary of material modifications ("SMM") made to Plan 1 and Plan 2 (the "Plans"). The Plans
provide pension benefits and also fund retiree medical benefits for eligible employees and their
dependents. This document should be retained with your Summary Plan Descriptions.
This SMM clarifies the optical coverage available to employees and dependents who are eligible for
retiree medical benefits under the Plans.
Optical Coverage
Optical coverage is provided to all Salaried Employees who are eligible for retiree medical benefits
under the Plans and who choose to enroll in the Kaiser Foundation Health Plan medical plan. As
explained in the "How Retiree Medical Coverage Works" section of your SPD, you also have the option
to choose the Preferred Provider Option (PPO) medical plan, which does not include optical coverage.

About This Summary

This document is the summary plan description ("SPD") for The Permanente Contribution Plan
of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc., also known as "Plan 2." As an SPD, this document is a
summary of the plan provisions. If there is any difference between the language in this summary
and that in the official plan document, the language in the official document rules.

While The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. ("TPMG") expects the plan to continue to be a part
of the members' benefit program, it reserves the right to amend, merge, modify, or terminate the
plan, in whole or in part, at any time.

In addition, TPMG does not promise that any medical benefits included in the plan will continue
to be offered. TPMG reserves the right to reduce, eliminate, and add or increase the amount of
required or optional member and beneficiary contributions, at any time and for any reason.

Participation in the plan does not give you rights to any benefit except as expressly provided in
the plan. Also, participation in the plan does not:

     give you rights to continued employment by TPMG,

     in any way prohibit changes in the terms of your employment, and

     in any way limit TPMG's right to terminate your employment for any reason.
Plan 2 for Salaried Employees

This is the summary plan description ("SPD") for The Permanente Contribution Plan of The
Permanente Medical Group, Inc., as amended and restated effective August 17, 2015 and last
amended December 13, 2019. This plan allows The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. ("TPMG")
to make contributions to an account that you manage. This plan is known informally as "Plan 2"
and is also referred to as "the plan" in this SPD.

This version of the SPD is for eligible Salaried employees employed with The Permanente
Medical Group, Inc. ("TPMG"). Participants in the plan are called "members."

This SPD describes the main features of the plan affecting members' benefits and explains the
terms of the plan. The SPD is organized to help you find the information you want quickly.

3  Benefits Effective December 13, 2019
Benefits at a Glance

Plan 2 works with The Retirement Plan for Physicians and Salaried Employees of TPMG ("Plan 1") and TPMG
Salary Deferral Plan ("Plan 3") to provide eligible participants with a comprehensive retirement benefits package.

      Plan 1 provides a traditional pension plan benefit, generally payable as a monthly benefit for your lifetime.
      Plan 2 is the plan under which TPMG makes contributions that you manage and invest.
      Plan 3 is a 401(k) plan that allows you to set aside savings for the future on a tax-advantaged basis and

          manage the investments.

The following are some highlights of the provisions of Plan 2:

Eligibility and  You become eligible to participate in the plan on the first day of the calendar quarter after
Enrollment       you complete two years of service starting on your hire date.

                 Once you meet the eligibility requirements, you are automatically enrolled in the plan.

                 For details, see "Eligibility and Enrollment" on page 5.

Plan             TPMG makes contributions to your account for each year in which you are a plan member.
Contributions    The amount of the contribution is:

                       7% of your compensation, up to the Social Security Wage Base (SSWB) ($137,700
                           for 2020) plus

                       10% of your compensation over the SSWB up to the compensation limit under
                           federal law ($285,000 for 2020)

                 For details, see "Plan Contributions" on page 8.

Vesting          You are always 100% vested.

                 Being vested means you have a non-forfeitable right to the benefits you have earned under
                 the plan.

                 For details, see "Vesting" on page 9.

When You Can     You can receive your benefits when you retire, terminate your employment with TPMG and
Receive Your     Mid-Atlantic Permanente Medical Group, P.C. ("MAPMG"), or you stop working because
Benefits         you become disabled.

                 You can defer benefits, but payment must begin by April 1 of the year following the later of:

                       the calendar year in which you reach age 72, or
                       the calendar year in which you retire from TPMG and MAPMG.

                 For details, see "When You Can Receive Your Benefits" on page 11.

How Your         You can choose to receive your benefits from the following options:

                       partial distributions
                       periodic installments
                       for single members, a single life annuity
                       for married members, a joint and survivor annuity

                 For details, see "How Your Benefits Can Be Paid" on page 11.

Taking a Loan     You may borrow from your account and repay the funds with interest.

                  The minimum loan amount is $1,000, and the maximum is the lesser of:

                        $50,000, less the amount of any other outstanding loans from the plan and all other
                            qualified plans maintained by TPMG or MAPMG during the 12-month period prior
                            to the new loan, or

                        half of your account balance.

                  You may not have more than two outstanding loans at a time, including and not limited to
                  loans you may have taken from the Salary Deferral Plan ("Plan 3").

                  In general, all loans must be repaid within five years. However, you have up to 15 years to
                  repay loans taken to purchase your primary residence.

                  For details, see "Loans" on page 12.

                  receive benefits.

Eligibility and Enrollment

Plan 2 participants are called "members."

This section describes who is eligible for membership in the plan and when membership begins and ends. It also
includes important information on designating a beneficiary to receive any survivor benefits that may be payable in
the event of your death.

Eligibility

Generally, your job designation determines if you are eligible to participate in Plan 2. All TPMG employees with the
job designation of salaried employee including Exempt and Nonunion Nonexempt ("NUNE") are eligible to become
members in the plan, with the exceptions described below.

You are eligible for Plan 2 membership if you are a salaried employee. A salaried employee is any employee of
TPMG who:

      is paid on a salaried basis,
      is a nonexempt employee,
      is classified by TPMG as a Physician Assistant, or
      is classified as an On-Call employee.

Not Eligible

You are not eligible if you:

      are covered by a collective bargaining agreement, unless the agreement specifically provides for
          participation in this plan,

      participate in another qualified retirement plan or individual retirement account or annuity that TPMG
          contributes to, other than The Retirement Plan for Physicians and Salaried Employees of TPMG ("Plan 1")
          or TPMG Salary Deferral Plan ("Plan 3"), or

      are a leased employee.

5                 Benefits Effective December 13, 2019
 Who is an On-Call Employee?

 An On-Call employee is a salaried or non-union, nonexempt employee other than a physician who, in lieu of
 benefits, receives a pay differential and includes:

        a short-hour employee (you are regularly scheduled to work less than 20 hours per week),
        a casual employee (you work on an intermittent basis), and
        a temporary employee (you were hired as an interim replacement or for temporary work on a

            predetermined work schedule for less than three calendar months).

When Membership Begins: Automatic Enrollment

Effective April 1, 2019, if you are eligible, your membership begins automatically on the first day of the calendar
quarter after two years of eligibility service, starting on your hire date.

 Example

 For example, suppose you begin work with TPMG on February 14, 2019 and work continuously until February
 14, 2021. You will have two years of eligibility service by February 14, 2021. You will become a member in the
 plan on April 1, 2021, the first day of the calendar quarter following February 14, 2021.

If you previously worked at a Medical Care Organization ("MCO") and transfer to TPMG, your service at the MCO
will count towards your Plan 2 participation requirements.
If you had service as a leased employee through a third party that had a contract with The Permanente Medical
Group, Inc. ("TPMG") or Mid-Atlantic Permanente Medical Group ("MAPMG"), you may be eligible for additional
service towards eligibility for Plan 2 contributions. This service will not count towards eligibility for retiree medical
benefits. To be credited with the additional service, you must have worked at least 1,500 hours during a 12-month
period; submit sufficient evidence that you performed work at TPMG or MAPMG and submit a claim for such
additional service within two years of the date this SPD or other notice, if earlier, was provided to you that service
as a leased employee can be taken into account for Plan purposes. If you do not submit a claim within the stipulated
two-year time period, any service as a leased employee will not be counted.

 What Is an MCO?

 "MCO" stands for Medical Care Organization and generally includes Kaiser Foundation Health Plan, Inc.
 ("KFHP") and related organizations, the Permanente Federation and other Permanente Medical Groups. MCO
 only includes organizations listed in the official plan document.

Military Leave

The plan complies with the provisions of the Uniformed Services Employment and Reemployment Rights Act of
1994 ("USERRA"). If you serve in qualifying military service and you return to work within the timeframes prescribed
by USERRA, the time you are on leave may be counted toward meeting your eligibility requirements.

Benefits Effective December 13, 2019  6
Designating a Beneficiary

When you become a member of the plan, you should name a beneficiary or beneficiaries to receive any plan benefits
that may be payable in case of your death. To name a beneficiary, you need to complete the appropriate plan
beneficiary designation form and return it to Plan Administrator. Any beneficiary designation made by you must be
received by Plan Administrator prior to your death to be valid.

Non-Spouse Beneficiaries

If you are married and you want to name someone other than your spouse as your primary beneficiary, including
naming a trust or your estate, your spouse must provide written consent to your beneficiary designation. Your
spouse's consent must:

      be on a form provided by the plan,
      be witnessed by a Notary Public, and
      acknowledge an understanding of the effect of the consent.
If you marry after designating a non-spouse beneficiary, your designation of your non-spouse beneficiary will no
longer be valid. Your new spouse will automatically be your beneficiary unless you elect otherwise.

 Definitions of "Married" and "Spouse"

 For all purposes of the plan, "married" means having a spouse and "spouse" means the person who is recognized
 as your spouse in accordance with laws of the State, the District of Columbia, a United States territory or a foreign
 jurisdiction. In accordance with applicable federal law, "spouse" does not include a domestic partner or a party
 to a civil union. Therefore, if you want your domestic partner to be your primary beneficiary, you will have to file
 a valid beneficiary designation form with Plan Administrator.

If You Die Without a Designated Beneficiary

If you die and Plan Administrator does not have a valid beneficiary designation on file for you, any benefits will be
payable to the person or persons in the first of the following classes that survive you:

      spouse;
      natural and adopted children and issue of deceased natural and adopted children by right of representation;
      parents; or
      your estate.
If you die without a valid beneficiary designation, your full account balance must be paid no later than December
31 following the fifth anniversary of your death.

Death of Beneficiary Prior to Beneficiary's Account Distribution

If you die and your designated beneficiary dies before the beneficiary's account balance is fully distributed, the
remaining account balance will be paid to your beneficiary's estate.

7  Benefits Effective December 13, 2019
 Is Your Beneficiary Designation Valid?

 Your beneficiary designation may be invalid for a number of reasons, such as:
  you do not name a beneficiary;
  the beneficiary you name does not survive you;
  the beneficiary designation filed is vague or ambiguous;
  the designated beneficiary cannot be reasonably identified; or
  the Plan Administrator does not receive a signed and dated beneficiary designation form before your death.
 You are encouraged to review your beneficiary designation(s) on file with Plan Administrator periodically and
 update the beneficiary designation form as needed. To designate a beneficiary, you can request the appropriate
 plan beneficiary designation form from Plan Administrator. You must return the form to Plan Administrator.

When Membership Ends

Your membership in Plan 2 ends when the earliest of the following events occurs:
      you have received a total distribution of your account, or
      your death.

Your Account

As a Plan 2 member, an account is maintained in your name, and contributions that TPMG makes on your behalf
are held in this account for your benefit. This account also reflects any investment earnings and losses, as well as
any fees that may be associated with your investment selections.

Plan Contributions

TPMG makes all contributions to Plan 2 on your behalf. You are not required or permitted to contribute to the plan.

TPMG will contribute:

      7% of your compensation, up to the Social Security Wage Base (SSWB) ($137,700 for 2020), plus
      10% of your compensation over the SSWB up to the compensation limit under federal law ($285,000 for

          2020).

Contribution Example

Suppose your compensation for 2020 is $150,000. Here's how the Plan 2 contributions from TPMG would be
calculated:

7% of your compensation, up to the Social Security Wage Base      7% x $137,700 =                $9,639
($137,700 for 2020)                                               10% x ($150,000 - $137,700) =  $1,230

10% of your compensation that exceeds the Social Security Wage
Base, up to the limit on eligible compensation under federal law
($285,000 for 2020)

Total                                                                                            $10,869

Benefits Effective December 13, 2019                                                                      8
 Definitions of "Compensation," "Social Security Wage Base," and "Eligible Compensation Limit"

 Compensation
 Under Plan 2, your compensation means your base pay plus annual incentive bonuses, and benefits paid in lieu
 of group health coverage paid during the contribution period. Your contributions to Plan 3 will not affect the
 compensation taken into account to determine your Plan 2 contributions.
 Social Security Wage Base
 Social Security limits the amount of income that is subject to Social Security's Old-Age, Survivors, and Disability
 Insurance ("OASDI") taxes. The limit is called the Social Security Wage Base.
 The Social Security Wage Base for 2020 is $137,700.
 The Wage Base is adjusted annually by the Social Security Administration.
 Eligible Compensation Limit
 Federal law sets a limit on how much compensation can be covered under tax-qualified plans such as Plan 2.
 The eligible compensation limit for 2020 is $285,000. The amount is subject to annual IRS cost of living
 adjustments.

When Contributions Are Made

TPMG makes contributions each payroll period for every plan member who is eligible to receive a contribution for
that payroll period.

If You Are on Military Leave

If you go on active military leave while employed by TPMG and you are a member of Plan 2, you may be entitled
to contributions after you return from military leave. You are eligible for these contributions if you are re-employed
by TPMG within the timeframes prescribed by USERRA. Your contribution will be based on the compensation you
would have received while you were on leave. If this amount is not clear, your contribution will be based on your
12-month average compensation earned immediately before your leave began.

Vesting

You are always 100% vested in your account.
Being vested means that you have a non-forfeitable right to your account.

9  Benefits Effective December 13, 2019

Initial Investments

When you become a plan member, you will receive information on your investment options from Fidelity. To make
your initial investments, contact the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015, or log
on to Fidelity's website at www.netbenefits.com/TPMG. You will need to establish login credentials and a password
for future transactions.

If you do not make an investment election, your contributions will be invested in the BlackRock LifePath Fund with
the date closest to your 65th birthday, which is the qualified default investment alternative designated by the
Retirement Program Committee.

Changing Your Investments

You may change your investment mix or transfer your investments between funds at any time. Contact the TPMG
Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015 or log on to www.netbenefits.com/TPMG. If your
transaction is confirmed before 1 p.m. Pacific time, it will take place on the same day. If your transaction is confirmed
after 1 p.m. Pacific time, it will take place the next day.

Benefits Effective December 13, 2019                                                                              10
Accessing Your Benefits

This section describes when and how your benefits can be paid.
It also describes:

           how you can take loans from your account,
           the benefits provided in case of your death, and
           how to apply for benefits.

When You Can Receive Your Benefits

Your account balance is payable to you when the earliest of the following occurs:

           you stop working for TPMG and MAPMG (note: depending on your age and circumstances at the time
                of withdrawal, you may be subject to a 10% federal tax penalty for early withdrawal ­ please refer to
                the section under "Taxes on Plan Benefits" on page 16), or

           you stop working because you become disabled (as determined by (1) TPMG's long term disability
                insurance carrier or (2) Social Security Administration and entitled to Social Security Disability
                Insurance benefits).

 Deferring Benefits

 You can defer benefits, but payment must begin by your Required Beginning Date.
 Your Required Beginning Date is the later of April 1 of the first calendar year following the later of:

             the year in which you reach age 72 (age 70 ˝ if you were born on or before June 30, 1949); or
             the year in which you stop working for TPMG and MAPMG.

How Your Benefits Can Be Paid

You have the choice of several payment forms, including:

           lump sum
           partial distributions
           periodic installments over a period of time not to exceed your life expectancy, as elected by you, and

                paid at least once a year
           single life annuity (if you are not married)
           qualified joint and 100% survivor annuity or a 50% or 66-2/3% joint and survivor annuity (if you are

                married)
Your benefits will be paid in the form of a single life annuity (if you are not married) or a joint and 100% survivor
annuity (if you are married) if you do not elect a different form of payment and the plan is required to pay benefits
to you. Also, if you are married and wish to choose a payment form other than the qualified joint and 100% survivor
annuity, you need your spouse's written notarized consent.
If your account balance is $1,000 or less, it will automatically be paid in one lump sum, regardless of your marital
status.
Your plan distribution(s) are taxable. See the section called "Taxes on Plan Benefits" on page 16 for more
information.

Lump Sum

With the lump sum payment option, you receive your entire account balance in one payment. No further benefit is
then payable.

11  Benefits Effective December 13, 2019
Partial Distributions

With the partial distribution payment option, you receive partial withdrawals (up to one per calendar quarter) before
you begin to receive another optional form of payment described in this section.

Periodic Installments

With the periodic installments payment option, you receive installment payments made at least once per year. Once
payments begin, you may elect to receive one additional payment each calendar quarter.

Annuities

With the annuity payment options, your entire account balance will be used to purchase an annuity that pays monthly
benefit payments to you for your lifetime and, if you are married, pays the same or a reduced monthly benefit for
your spouse's lifetime.

If you are not married, your annuity option is a single life annuity, which is a monthly payment for your lifetime only
with no survivor benefit. Unmarried members are not eligible for joint and survivor annuity options.
If you are married, you may choose a 50%, 66-2/3% or 100% joint and survivor annuity option. With these options,
your account balance is used to purchase an annuity that pays you a monthly benefit for your lifetime, with 50%,
66-2/3%, or 100% of that amount continuing to your surviving spouse for their lifetime. Married members are not
eligible for the single life annuity option.

Election Period

Any election regarding the time and form of payment of your retirement benefits must be made during your election
period, which is within the 90-day period before your benefits begin, and must be made in the form and manner
designated by the Plan Administrator. You may revoke your election at any time before you start receiving benefits.
You will not be allowed to revoke your election or change the payment form after you start receiving benefits.

Direct Rollover

You (or your spousal beneficiary) may roll over a plan distribution into another employer's qualified retirement plan,
403(b) plan or governmental 457(b) plan that accepts rollovers, or into an individual retirement account or annuity
("IRA"), including a Roth IRA. The rollover must be a direct rollover, meaning the distribution is made directly from
this plan to the trustee or custodian of the other plan or IRA. A designated beneficiary other than your spouse may
roll over a plan distribution into an inherited IRA.

Certain types of payments are not eligible for rollover. You can roll over lump sum distributions and partial
distributions, but you cannot roll over periodic distributions, such as installment payments or annuity payments, or
minimum required distributions. The minimum direct rollover amount is $500. When you choose to receive a
distribution, you will receive more detailed information about tax consequences and the rollover rules.

Loans

You may borrow from your account and repay the funds with interest.

The minimum loan amount is $1,000, and the maximum is the lesser of:

      $50,000, less the amount of any other outstanding loans from the plan and all other qualified plans
          maintained by TPMG or MAPMG during the 12-month period prior to the new loan, or

      half of your account balance in the plan.

You may not have more than two outstanding loans at a time, including loans you may have taken from Plan 3.

The interest rate on the loan will be based on the prime interest rate plus one percent.

Benefits Effective December 13, 2019  12
All loans must be repaid within five years, although loans to purchase a home that will be your principal residence
may be repaid over a maximum period of 15 years.

Applying for a Loan

To apply for a loan, contact the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015. You will
be provided with detailed information about plan loans, including current interest rates, any costs relating to taking
out a loan, and the terms for repayment. You can also log on to www.netbenefits.com/TPMG to download loan
forms. You must return all completed forms to Fidelity.
If you are married, your spouse must provide written notarized consent to the loan. This consent must be provided
within 90 days before the loan goes into effect.

Repaying Your Loan

In general, loans will be repaid through payroll deductions. Repayments will be made directly to the account from
which the funds were borrowed and will be invested according to your current investment elections.
If you stop working with TPMG, or if you become disabled or die, before your loan is repaid, your account will be
reduced by the amount of the outstanding loan unless you agree to a repayment schedule. The outstanding loan
balance, including interest, will be considered a distribution from the plan and subject to the appropriate income
taxes. You may choose, however, to repay the loan balance in full, instead of having it treated as a distribution.
If you do not repay your loan as scheduled, you will be considered in default, and you will be prohibited from taking
another loan from Plan 2 and Plan 3 until after a period of time equal to the term of the defaulted loan.
If you are on military leave, you do not have to repay your loan until you return to active employment with TPMG.

Benefits If You Die

Upon your death, your account balance will be payable to your beneficiary. In the event of the subsequent death of
your beneficiary, any unpaid account balance will be paid to the estate of your beneficiary.
Your beneficiary may elect one of the following payment methods. If you are married and your spouse is your
beneficiary, the payment method will be the Qualified Pre-retirement Survivor Annuity, unless you waived this
payment form or your spouse elects another payment form.

      Lump Sum: Your beneficiary receives your entire account balance in one payment. No further benefit is
          payable.

      Installments: Your beneficiary receives installment payments made at least once per year, not to exceed
          their life expectancy. Once payments begin, your beneficiary may elect to receive one additional payment
          each calendar quarter.

      Qualified Pre-retirement Survivor Annuity: Your full account balance is used to purchase an annuity that
          provides monthly payments to your spouse for their lifetime.
          You may waive this benefit form with your spouse's written consent. If you waive this benefit before age 35,
          your waiver will expire when you reach age 35 and you will need to complete a new waiver with your
          spouse's written consent.

 Direct Rollover

 Your beneficiary may be eligible to roll over your account balance to another plan or IRA. See "Direct Rollover"
 on page 12 for more information about rollovers.

13  Benefits Effective December 13, 2019
Applying for Benefits

To request a distribution of benefits from your plan account, call the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service
Center at 1-800-889-4015 or log on to www.netbenefits.com/TPMG. Fidelity can provide you or your beneficiary
with the necessary benefit application, election and tax forms and guide you through the application process. You
must complete all required forms and file them with Fidelity before any benefits can be paid to you. Application
forms are not considered filed until they are received by Fidelity.

To apply for retiree medical benefits, call the Kaiser Permanente Retirement Center (KPRC) at 1-866-627-2826 or
log onto www.ibenefitcenter.com/kp. See "Retiree Medical Benefits" on page 17 for information.

A claim for benefits must be made in writing within 360 days after payment of the claimed benefit is due.

Denied Claims

If your application or other claim for benefits is denied, in whole or in part, the TPMG Benefits Manager (or designee)
will notify you in writing or electronically of the denial within a reasonable period of time of no more than 90 days
after the plan receives your claim.

If due to special circumstances additional time is required to consider and respond to your claim, you will be notified
in writing before the expiration of the initial 90-day period and the time for responding to your claim may be extended
up to an additional 90 days. The notice will describe the special circumstances requiring the extension, including
whether additional information is required to decide your claim, and the date by which the TPMG Benefits Manager
(or designee) expects to make a determination.

If your claim concerns your disability and the claim is denied, the notice of denial described above will be provided
within 45 days (not 90 days) and if special circumstances require an extension of time to respond to your claim, the
extension will be no more than 30 days. The TPMG Benefits Manager may further extend this period for up to an
additional 30 days by notifying you in writing before the end of the first 30-day extension.

A notice of claim denial will:

      State the specific reasons why the claim is denied;
      Identify the specific plan provisions on which the denial is based;
      Describe any additional material or information that is required before the claim can be approved, and why

          that information is needed;
      Explain the steps that you need to take (and the applicable time limits) to appeal the denial of your claim

          and your right to bring civil action under section 502(a) of ERISA if you file an appeal and your appeal is
          denied;
      State the time limits described below for initiating any legal action involving a benefit claim.

This notice will include additional information if your claim concerns your disability and is denied in whole or in part
based on a finding that you are not disabled, including (a) a discussion of the decision including the basis for
disagreeing with the views of any healthcare, medical or vocational professionals who evaluated you or whose
advice was obtained in connection with your appeal, (b) a statement that information concerning scientific or clinical
judgments relating to the decision will be provided upon request, (c) any rules, guidelines, protocols, standards or
similar criteria relied upon in making the determination or a statement that none exist, (d) a statement that you are
entitled to receive, upon request and free of charge, reasonable access to and copies of all documents, records
and other information relevant to your claim. The notice will be provided in a culturally and linguistically appropriate
manner. Details concerning such additional information are set out in Section 10.3 of the plan document which is
available upon request.

You may consider your claim denied and proceed to the appeal stage described below if the TPMG Benefits
Manager (or designee) does not respond to your claim within 90 days (45 days if your claim is for disability benefits).
If you do not file a timely appeal, the TPMG Benefits Manager's (or designee's) decision will be final,
binding, and conclusive on all concerned and you will not have the right to bring a civil action under section
502(a) of ERISA.

Benefits Effective December 13, 2019  14
Review of Denied Claims/Filing an Appeal

If your claim is denied in whole or in part, you may appeal the denial. To appeal a denied claim, you, your beneficiary,
or your authorized representative must file a written appeal with:

          Administrative Committee
          MD Benefits
          1800 Harrison Street, 7th Floor
          Oakland, CA 94612

You must file your appeal within 60 days (180 days if your claim is for disability benefits) of the date you received
the denial notice. You should explain the basis for your appeal and submit any relevant written comments,
documents, records, or other information.

You will be provided, upon request and free of charge, reasonable access to, and copies of, all documents, records,
and other information relevant to your request for appeal.

A document, record, or other information is considered relevant to the claim if it:

      was relied on in making the benefit decision,
      was submitted, considered, or generated in the course of making the benefit decision (without regard to

          whether it was relied on in making the decision), or
      demonstrates compliance with the requirement that benefit decisions follow the terms of the plan and be

          consistently applied to similarly situated claimants.

Appeal Process

The Administrative Committee will decide your appeal within a reasonable period of time, but no later than 60 days
(45 days if your claim is for disability benefits) after it receives your appeal. However, the Administrative Committee
may need more time -- up to 120 days (90 days if your claim is for disability benefits) after it receives your appeal
-- to make a decision due to special circumstances. If an extension of time is required because of special
circumstances, you will be given written notice of the extension before the expiration of the initial determination
period. The written extension notice will indicate the special circumstances requiring the extension and the date by
which the committee expects to render a decision.

The Administrative Committee will consider all comments, documents, records, and other information that you have
submitted in reviewing your claim, regardless of whether that information was considered in determining your initial
claim.

If your claim is for disability benefits, the review will not defer to the original denial and will be decided by the
Administrative Committee. If your claim was denied based on medical judgment, the Administrative Committee will
consult with a health care professional, who has training and experience in the particular medical field involved, and
who is different from the person, or their subordinate, who was consulted in connection with the denial of your initial
claim.

The Administrative Committee will also identify any medical or vocational expert whose advice was obtained in
connection with the denial of your initial claim (without regard to whether the advice was relied upon in denying your
claim) upon request. The Administrative Committee will provide you, free of charge, with any new or additional
evidence generated, considered or relied upon in deciding your appeal, and any new or additional rationale on
which its decision may be based. This information will be provided to you as soon as possible so that you have
time to respond before the Administrative Committee must decide your appeal.

Denied Appeals

If your appeal is denied in whole or in part, the Administrative Committee (or designee) will notify you in writing or
electronically within a reasonable period of time. This notice of the denial of your appeal will include:

      the specific reasons for the denial;
      the specific plan provisions on which the denial is based;

15  Benefits Effective December 13, 2019
      a statement that you are entitled to receive, upon request and free of charge, reasonable access to, and
          copies of, all documents, records, and other information relevant to your claim (a document is considered
          relevant if it meets one or more of the criteria listed at the end of the "Review of Denied Claims/Filing an
          Appeal" section, under "Denied Claims" on page 15);

      a statement of your right to bring a civil action under ERISA section 502(a) following a denial of your appeal;
      the time limits described below for initiating any legal action involving a benefit claim.

If your appeal concerns your disability and is denied in whole or in part based on a finding that you are not disabled,
this notice will also include: (a) a discussion of the decision including the basis for disagreeing with the views of any
healthcare, medical or vocational professionals who evaluated you or whose advice was obtained in connection
with your appeal, (b) a statement that information concerning scientific or clinical judgments relating to the decision
will be provided upon request, (c) any rules, guidelines, protocols, standards or similar criteria relied upon in making
the determination or a statement that none exist. The notice will be provided in a culturally and linguistically
appropriate manner. Details concerning such additional information are set out in Section 10.3 of the plan document
which is available upon request.

If you do not receive notice of the denial of your appeal within the time allowed, you may consider your appeal
denied. Decisions by the Administrative Committee are final, binding, and conclusive on all concerned and
shall be given the maximum possible deference allowed by law.

The Administrative Committee has discretionary authority to make findings of fact and to interpret and apply the
terms of the plan in connection with claims and appeals.

You may not initiate a lawsuit to obtain plan benefits until after you have exhausted the claims and appeals
procedures described above. No lawsuit may be initiated more than 360 days after the claims and appeals
procedures described above have been exhausted. Any lawsuit concerning the Plan must be brought in the United
States District Court for the Northern District of California.

The specific procedures governing claims for medical benefits (including, but not limited to, procedures for urgent
care claims, concurrent care decisions, pre-service and post-service claims, procedures for filing claim forms,
providing notifications of benefit determinations, and reviewing denied claims) applicable to the medical plans
sponsored by TPMG are provided to you automatically, and free of charge, as a separate document.

Taxes on Plan Benefits

The plan is designed to meet Internal Revenue Code ("IRC") requirements as a "qualified plan," to take advantage
of special tax treatment available to qualified plans. This means that:

      contributions to the plan are not currently taxable to you; and
      the investment gains are not currently taxable to you or TPMG.

You will be taxed only when you actually receive benefits from the plan. Such payments will generally be taxable
as ordinary income in the year received. When you elect to receive a distribution from the plan, the recordkeeper
will provide you with a written notice that describes the tax consequences of the available payment options in more
detail.

If you receive a lump sum, you should be aware that federal tax withholding up to 20% of your account balance is
deducted from the payment you receive from the plan. Your account balance is taxed as ordinary income in the
year you receive it and, depending on your age and circumstances, may also be subject to a 10% federal tax penalty
for early withdrawal.

You can defer the payment of income taxes and avoid the 20% withholding and any applicable penalty by instructing
the Fidelity to roll over the eligible balance directly into another qualified plan or an individual retirement account
("IRA").

Another option is for you to receive your account balance and then roll it over yourself into another qualified plan or
IRA within 60 days from the date of receipt. In this case, you defer income taxes, but the 20% withholding is still
deducted from the plan payment. As a result, only 80% of your account balance is available to be rolled over, and
the remaining 20% would be taxable. To roll over an amount equal to 100% of your account balance and defer

Benefits Effective December 13, 2019  16
taxes on the full amount of your account balance, you will need to use other money to replace the 20% that was
withheld by the plan.

The tax rules that apply to this plan are complex and may apply differently to each individual. Therefore, the
recordkeeper and the Plan Administrator cannot advise you on your taxes and encourages you to consult your own
tax advisor regarding the treatment of payments made to you.
