Eligibility and Enrollment

This section describes the eligibility requirements for retiree medical benefits provided by this plan and how to enroll
in or change coverage.

If you are eligible for post-retirement medical benefits and you and your eligible dependents are under age 65, no
form is necessary to enroll in coverage. You should call the KPRC at 1-866-627-2826 to confirm your coverage
before you retire.

If you are eligible for post-retirement medical benefits and you or your eligible dependents are age 65 or older or
eligible for Medicare, you must complete an enrollment form and return the form (along with any other requested
materials) to the KPRC at P.O. Box 9022, Providence, RI 02940-4022.

If you decide you do not want to participate, you need to send a letter to that effect to the KPRC at the address
above.

Cost of Coverage

TPMG makes contributions to a trust for post-retirement medical benefits. The contributions are deposited in a
separate account under the plan where they are held by the plan trustee for the sole benefit of eligible plan
members and eligible dependents. At this time, the plan does not require contributions from retirees who are
eligible for post-retirement medical benefits.

17                        Benefits Effective December 13, 2019
Eligibility

To qualify for retiree medical benefits under this plan, you must terminate employment as a salaried employee of
TPMG on or after age 55 with at least 15 years of vesting service. Grandfathered employees who do not meet this
requirement can also qualify if the sum of their age and years of service is at least 75 at the time of termination (see
section below regarding grandfathered employees).

A year of vesting service for this purpose means a 12-month period in which you work 1,000 hours. Please note
that if you retire on or after January 1, 2019, you must have at least three consecutive years of employment as a
salaried employee of TPMG in the last 10 years before your retirement.

If you are eligible for Medicare, you must also enroll in Medicare Parts A and B and the Kaiser Permanente Senior
Advantage plan or a Preferred Provider Organization Plan offered to Medicare-eligible retirees. A limited group of
retirees receive alternative forms of coverage, such as coverage under the Traditional Kaiser Permanente health
plan.

If you are not an eligible salaried employee of TPMG at the time your employment ends, you will not receive retiree
medical benefits from this plan; however, you may be eligible under the retiree medical plan applicable to your
employee group. See "Eligibility and Enrollment" on page 17 to determine if you are an eligible salaried employee.
You may also contact the KPRC at 1-866-627-2826 for information about the retiree medical benefits available to
your employee group.

When Coverage Begins

Your retiree medical coverage under this plan will begin when you become eligible for and enroll in Medicare
(typically this occurs at age 65). Your coverage includes basic medical, supplemental medical, and vision coverage.

Grandfathered Employees

You are a grandfathered employee if you were hired by TPMG or another MCO before February 1, 1986 and you
have not had a break in service (see below regarding breaks in service).

If you are a grandfathered employee, your coverage may begin before you become eligible for Medicare.
Grandfathered employees who meet the age and service requirements described above are eligible for basic
medical, supplemental medical, dental and vision coverage, and Medicare Part B standard premium
reimbursements, upon termination of employment with TPMG and all MCOs.

 Have I had a Break-in-Service?

 A break in service occurs when you terminate employment with TPMG (and all other MCOs) before you meet
 the age and service requirements for retiree medical benefits under this plan (or another retiree medical plan
 offered by another MCO). However, a termination of employment does not count as a break in service if at the
 time of termination you had at least two years of service in a benefits-eligible position, and within two years after
 that termination you return to employment in a benefits-eligible non-union position with TPMG or another MCO.

 For example, suppose you were first hired on June 1, 1984 and worked continuously in a benefits-eligible position
 until terminating employment with TPMG on June 1, 2000 at age 54 with 16 years of service. If you were rehired
 in a benefits-eligible non-union position on or before May 31, 2002, you would not have a break in service, and
 you would remain a "grandfathered" employee. However, if you were rehired by TPMG more than two years
 after June 1, 2000 (for example, June 1, 2004), you would have a break in service, and you would no longer be
 a "grandfathered" employee.

Benefits Effective December 13, 2019  18
Available Medical Coverage

If you meet the requirements for retiree medical coverage (see "Eligibility" on page 18), you and your eligible
dependents will be enrolled in one of two medical plans. Your eligible dependents will be covered under the same
plan as you. The two medical plans are:

      Kaiser Foundation Health Plan High Option Plan (KFHP) -- this is the same plan offered to active
          employees.

      Preferred Provider Organization (PPO) Plan -- this is the same PPO Plan that is offered to active
          employees.

Your KFHP coverage will include supplemental medical plan coverage.

Your coverage (KFHP or PPO) is subject to change when the active group coverage changes.

There are no pre-existing condition exclusions.

For additional information on the retiree medical plans, contact the KPRC at 1-866-627-2826.

Changing Covered Dependents

If you have a qualifying family status change after retirement that is listed below, your change must be reported to
the KPRC within 31 days of the event:

      your marriage, divorce, legal separation;
      the birth or adoption of a child;
      death of a spouse or eligible dependent;
      a change in your spouse's coverage (including a change in your spouse's employment); or
      a change in the eligible status of your eligible dependent.

 Definition of an Eligible Child

 An eligible child is any child who (regardless of the financial relationship or dependency, residency, marital status,
 student status, employment, or any combination of these) is 26 or younger who is not covered by any other
 employer plan, or any child older than age 26 who prior to age 26 met the requirements of the KFHP, Inc.
 Evidence of Coverage, including being permanently and totally disabled and your dependent under IRS rules.

Effect of Divorce or Legal Separation on Coverage

Your spouse will cease to be eligible for retiree medical coverage upon your divorce or legal separation. You are
required to notify the KPRC of your divorce or legal separation within 60 days for your spouse (or former spouse)
to be eligible for COBRA continuation coverage. Failure to provide timely notification will jeopardize your spouse's
(or former spouse's) eligibility for COBRA continuation coverage.

Survivor Benefits

If you die, retiree medical coverage will continue to be provided to your eligible dependents for so long as they
remain eligible. Surviving spouse coverage ends upon remarriage. Coverage for eligible children ends at age 26.

Coverage May End If You Are Re-employed

Your retiree medical benefits under this plan may end if you are re-employed by TPMG or any other MCO. This
includes retiree medical benefits available to your eligible dependents and Medicare Part B premium
reimbursements.
If you are rehired into a non-benefited position, your retiree medical coverage will continue but any Medicare Part
B premium reimbursements for which you were eligible for will end.

19  Benefits Effective December 13, 2019
If you become eligible for benefits as an active employee of TPMG or any other MCO, all retiree medical benefits
under this plan will end. Your retiree medical benefits under this plan will resume when you re-retire unless you
have become eligible for retiree medical benefits under a different retiree medical program offered by TPMG or
another MCO.

Please note that no retiree medical coverage or other benefits are provided by this plan to any individual who is
eligible for retiree medical coverage under a different retiree medical plan or program offered by TPMG or any other
MCO.

Coordination with Medicare

Once you or your eligible dependents become eligible for Medicare (either because of age or disability), you/they
must enroll in Medicare Parts A and B to be eligible for any retiree medical coverage under this plan. If you have
KFHP coverage, you/they must also assign your Medicare benefits to KFHP and be enrolled in a Kaiser Permanente
Senior Advantage Plan. Your/their coverage may be terminated if you fail to enroll in Medicare or assign Medicare
benefits to KFHP.

Summary of Benefits

This SPD contains only a summary description of the eligibility requirements for retiree basic medical, supplemental
medical, dental, and vision coverage. Detailed schedules of these benefits are available from the KPRC, free of
charge, upon request.

Also, information covering the following is provided by the Plan Administrator in a separate document, free of
charge:

      deductibles, coinsurance, and copayment amounts for which you may be responsible,
      limits on benefits,
      preventative services that are covered,
      the extent to which existing or new drugs are covered,
      the extent to which medical tests are covered,
      provisions for network providers and the extent to which out-of-network coverage is provided,
      the conditions or limits on emergency care,
      provisions requiring preauthorization or utilization review, and
      a listing of network providers, if applicable.

Other Retiree Medical Information

This section includes information that affects your medical benefits.

Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act ("HIPAA")

The plan will use protected health information ("PHI") only to the extent it is permitted by the Health Insurance
Portability and Accountability Act of 1996 ("HIPAA"). Specifically, the plan will use and disclose protected health
information for purposes related to health care treatment, payment for health care, and health care operations.

COBRA Continuation

If you are not eligible for retiree medical benefits under the plan, you have a right to continuation coverage under
the Consolidated Omnibus Budget Reconciliation Act of 1985 ("COBRA").

COBRA continuation coverage can become available to you when you would otherwise lose your group health
coverage. It can also become available to other members of your family who are covered under the plan when they
would otherwise lose their group health coverage.

Benefits Effective December 13, 2019  20
Please refer to the "General Notice of COBRA Continuation Coverage Rights" previously provided to you for
additional information on when it may become available to you and your family and what you need to do to protect
your right to receive it. If you have any questions regarding COBRA continuation coverage and to provide notice to
TPMG as required to receive COBRA coverage, please contact the NHRSC at 1-877-457-4772.

HIPAA Special Enrollment Notice

If you decline retiree coverage for yourself or your eligible dependents (including your spouse) because you have
other health insurance coverage, you may be able to enroll yourself or your eligible dependents in the retiree medical
coverage under the plan if your other coverage ends. You must request to enroll in this plan within 31 days after
your other coverage ends.
In addition, if you have a new dependent as a result of marriage, birth, adoption, or placement for adoption, you
may be able to enroll yourself and your eligible dependents, provided that you request enrollment within 31 days
after such events.

Certificate of Creditable Coverage

You should be provided a certificate of creditable coverage, free of charge from the plan or health insurance issuer
when any of the following events occur:

      you lose coverage under the plan,
      you become entitled to elect COBRA continuation coverage, or
      your COBRA continuation coverage ceases, if you request it before losing coverage, or if you request it up

          to 24 months after losing coverage.
Without evidence of creditable coverage, you may be subject to a pre-existing condition exclusion for 12 months
(18 months for late enrollees) after your coverage enrollment date.

Contact Information

If you have any questions regarding retiree medical benefits, COBRA, or HIPAA, you may contact the KPRC at 1-
866-627-2826.
For more information about your rights under ERISA, as well as information about COBRA, HIPAA, and other laws
affecting group health plans, contact the nearest Regional or District Office of the U.S. Department of Labor's
Employee Benefits Security Administration ("EBSA") or visit the EBSA website at www.dol.gov/ebsa. (Addresses
and phone number of Regional and District EBSA Offices are available through EBSA's website.)

Other Rules and Regulations

This section describes additional rules and regulations that may affect your benefits, as well as your rights under
laws such as the Employee Retirement Income Security Act of 1974 (as amended), known as "ERISA."

Benefits Not Insured

The Pension Benefit Guaranty Corporation ("PBGC"), a federal insurance agency, insures certain types of benefits
under defined benefit plans. Because Plan 2 is a defined contribution money purchase pension plan and your
benefits are based on your Plan 2 account balance, benefits are not insured by the PBGC.

21  Benefits Effective December 13, 2019
Qualified Domestic Relations Order ("QDRO")

Generally, your benefits under the plan cannot be assigned, either voluntarily or involuntarily, except through a
qualified domestic relations order or "QDRO."

In the event of your divorce or another domestic relations matter, a QDRO may legally require the distribution of a
portion of your plan benefit to an alternate payee (your spouse, former spouse, child, or other dependent). Your
alternate payee may elect to receive an immediate distribution from the newly established account following the
qualification of the QDRO.

Your benefit will be reduced if a court has ordered that a portion of your total accrued benefit is to be paid to an
alternate payee under a QDRO.

You may obtain a free copy of the plan's QDRO procedures from the QDRO administrator by contacting QDRO
Consultants at 1-800-527-8481. You will also be provided with information describing your rights, plan benefits, and
how the determination process works.

If you have a pending domestic relations order, you may not begin to receive any distribution from the plan. If a
distribution has already started, a portion of the distribution may be withheld pending resolution of the QDRO review
process.

Potential Loss of Benefits

The plan is intended to provide you with a valuable retirement benefit. However, some individuals may not qualify
for a benefit and others may lose a benefit even if they once qualified. Circumstances resulting in a denial or loss
of benefits are discussed more fully elsewhere in this SPD. You should be aware that the following are some, but
not all, of the possible reasons you may not receive part or all of a benefit:

      If you do not meet the requirements for eligibility to participate, you will not be entitled to any benefit.
      If all or a portion of your benefits are awarded to an alternate payee pursuant to a QDRO, you will not

          receive your entire benefit.
      If the plan is terminated with insufficient assets to provide your benefit, then your benefit may be reduced

          or in some cases may be lost altogether.
      If the plan should be disqualified by the IRS, contributions made to the plan may result in current taxable

          income to you.

23  Benefits Effective December 13, 2019
Your ERISA Rights

As a member of the plan, you are entitled to certain rights and protections under the Employee Retirement Income
Security Act of 1974 ("ERISA"). ERISA provides that all plan participants shall have the following rights.

Receive Information about Your Plan and Benefits

ERISA provides that all plan participants shall be entitled to:

      Examine without charge, at the Plan Administrator's office, all documents governing the plan, including
          insurance contracts, and a copy of the latest annual report (Form 5500 Series) filed by the plan with the
          U.S. Department of Labor and available at the Public Disclosure Room of the Employee Benefits Security
          Administration.

      Obtain, upon written request to the Plan Administrator, copies of documents governing the operation of the
          plan, including insurance contracts, and copies of the latest annual report (Form 5500 Series) and updated
          summary plan description. The Plan Administrator may make a reasonable charge for the copies.

      Receive a summary of the plan's annual financial report. The Plan Administrator is required by law to furnish
          each plan member with a copy of this summary annual report.

      Obtain a statement telling you whether you have a right to receive a pension at normal retirement age, and
          if so, what your benefits would be at normal retirement age if you stop working under the plan now. If you
          do not have a right to a pension, the statement will tell you how many more years you have to work to get
          a right to a pension. This statement must be requested in writing and is not required to be given more than
          once every 12 months. The plan must provide the statement free of charge.

Prudent Actions by Plan Fiduciaries

In addition to creating rights for plan members, ERISA imposes duties upon the people who are responsible for the
operation of the plan. The people who operate your plan, called "fiduciaries" of the plan, have a duty to do so
prudently and in the interest of you, other plan members, and beneficiaries.

No one, including your employer or any other person, may fire you or otherwise discriminate against you in any way
to prevent you from obtaining a pension or welfare benefit or exercising your rights under ERISA.

Enforce Your Rights

If your claim for a benefit is denied or ignored, in whole or in part, you have a right to know why this was done, to
obtain copies of documents relating to the decision without charge, and to appeal any denial, all within certain time
schedules.

Under ERISA, there are steps you can take to enforce the above rights. For instance, if you request a copy of plan
documents or the latest annual report from the plan and do not receive them within 30 days, you may file suit in a
federal court. In such a case, the court may require the Plan Administrator to provide the materials and pay you up
to $110 a day until you receive the materials, unless the materials were not sent because of reasons beyond the
control of the Plan Administrator.

If you have a claim for benefits that is denied or ignored, in whole or in part, you may file suit in a state or federal
court. In addition, if you disagree with the plan's decision or lack thereof concerning the qualified status of a domestic
relations order, you may file suit in federal court. If it should happen that plan fiduciaries misuse the plan's money,
or if you are discriminated against for asserting your rights, you may seek assistance from the U.S. Department of
Labor, or you may file suit in a federal court. The court will decide who should pay costs and legal fees. If you are
successful, the court may order the person you have sued to pay these costs and fees. If you lose, the court may
order you to pay the costs and fees, if for example, it finds your claim is frivolous.

Benefits Effective December 13, 2019  24
Assistance with Your Questions

If you have any questions about your plan, you should contact the Plan Administrator. If you have any questions
about this statement or about your rights under ERISA, or if you need assistance in obtaining documents from the
Plan Administrator, you should contact the nearest Office of the Employee Benefits Security Administration, U.S.
Department of Labor, listed in your telephone directory or the Division of Technical Assistance and Inquiries,
Employee Benefits Security Administration, U.S. Department of Labor, 200 Constitution Avenue N.W., Washington,
D.C. 20210. You may also obtain certain publications about your rights and responsibilities under ERISA by calling
the publications hotline of the Employee Benefits Security Administration.

          SUMMARY OF MATERIAL MODIFICATIONS

To: Participants and Beneficiaries of the following retirement plans:

 The Permanente Contribution Plan of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. ("Plan 2")
 The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. Salary Deferral Plan ("Plan 3")

This is a summary of material modifications (SMM) to the retirement plans listed above (Plans). No
action is required. This SMM updates your Summary Plan Descriptions (SPDs) for these Plans and
should be retained with your SPDs. Specifically, this SMM describes changes to the tax laws governing
the timing of benefit payments to you and your beneficiaries and the availability of plan loans.

New Required Beginning Date for Required Minimum Distributions

When you stop working and if you are eligible, you can receive a distribution, or you may defer
payments no later than the date the Internal Revenue Service requires you to take a first withdrawal.
This is referred to as the Required Beginning Date (RBD) for Required Minimum Distributions (RMDs).
RMDs cannot be rolled over to an individual retirement account or other qualified retirement plan.

Previously, employees had to begin receiving RMDs from qualified retirement plans by April 1 of the
later of the calendar year following the year they reached age 70.5 or retired, which is the RBD. The
Setting Up Every Community for Retirement Enhancement Act (SECURE) increased the age from 70.5
to 72 for individuals who reached age 70.5 after December 31, 2019. The Plans have been updated to
reflect this change. You must begin receiving RMDs from the Plans by April 1 of the later of the calendar
year following the year you reach age 72 or retire from TPMG.

Required Minimum Distributions for Beneficiaries

Previously, the general distributions rules to beneficiaries of deceased participants required that full
account balance distributions take place no later than December 31 of the calendar year in which the
participant died; by December 31 of the calendar year in which the deceased participant would have
reached age 70; or by the end of the year of the 5th year after the participant died. The timing rules
varied depending on the beneficiary.

The SECURE Act changed the timing rules for distributions to most beneficiaries for participants who
die after December 31, 2019. In general, under the SECURE Act, most beneficiary account balances
must be fully distributed by the end of the 10th year after the year the participant dies. Special rules
apply to certain types of beneficiaries, including spouses, minor children, trusts and others. Plan 2 and
Plan 3 have been updated to reflect changes made by the SECURE Act.

No action is required. As always, you may designate a Plan beneficiary or change your Plan beneficiary
at any time. Contact MD Benefits at (510) 625-6600 if you wish to designate a beneficiary or review or
change your current Plan beneficiary designations.

If you have questions about how the SECURE Act changes may affect the timing of payments to your
beneficiaries, you should speak with a qualified estate planner or financial planner.
Temporary Changes Relating to COVID-19
Plan 2 and Plan 3 have been updated to reflect legislation that temporarily changed the rules relating
to retirement plan loans and distributions.
Temporary Increase to Maximum Plan Loan Limit
Plan 2 and Plan 3 allow you to borrow from your account balances and repay the funds with interest
by requesting up to two loans not to exceed the $50,000 combined plan loan maximum. Under the
Coronavirus Aid, Relief and Economic Security Act (CARES Act), the maximum plan loan temporarily
increased from $50,000 to $100,000 to eligible plan participants who experienced a financial loss due
to COVID-19, certified the need for financial assistance, and requested a Plan loan from May 1, 2020,
through September 23, 2020.
Temporary Option to Suspend Plan Loan Payments
Under the CARES Act, eligible plan participants who experienced a financial loss due to COVID-19 that
affected their ability to make timely loan payments and certified the need for financial assistance, had
the option to suspend the loan payments from April 20, 2020, through December 31, 2020.
Temporary Option to Suspend Minimum Required Distributions
Due to the significant market volatility caused by the COVID-19 pandemic, the CARES Act allowed
participants in Plan 2 and Plan 3 to elect to take Required Minimum Distributions (RMDs) or to
temporarily suspend the distributions for the 2020 plan year.
Temporary Option to Receive Early Plan Distribution due to Financial Loss (Plan 3 Only)
Under the CARES Act, eligible Plan 3 participants who experienced a financial loss due to the COVID-19
pandemic and certified the need for financial assistance, had the option to receive a distribution of up
to $100,000 during 2020 and to recontribute the full distribution to the plan over a three-year period.

If you have questions, please contact the National Human Resources Service Center at (877) 457-4772.
MD Benefits, The Permanente Medical Group, Inc.

The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. Salary Deferral Plan
EIN/Plan Number: 94-2728480/013

the plan. Also, participation in the plan does not:

     give you rights to continued employment by TPMG,

3  Benefits Effective December 31, 2021
Benefits at a Glance

Plan 3 is a 401(k) plan that allows you to set aside savings for the future on a tax-advantaged basis, and manage
their investment.

Plan 3 works with The Retirement Plan for Physicians and Salaried Employees of TPMG ("Plan 1") and The
Permanente Contribution Plan of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. ("Plan 2") to provide eligible physicians and
employees with a comprehensive retirement benefits package.

      Plan 1 provides a traditional pension plan benefit, generally payable as a monthly benefit for your lifetime.
      Plan 2 is the plan under which TPMG makes contributions that you manage and invest.
      Plan 3 is a 401(k) plan that allows you to set aside savings for the future on a tax-advantaged basis and

          manage the investments.

The following are some highlights of the provisions of Plan 3.

Eligibility and  You are eligible as of the first day of the month following your date of hire if you are a
Enrollment       physician or a salaried employee.

                 If you do not enroll within your first 30 days, you will be automatically enrolled in the plan,
                 with an opportunity to decline enrollment.

                 For details, see "Eligibility and Enrollment" on page 5.

Plan             The plan allows you to save for the future by making contributions that you manage and
Contributions    invest. There are several ways that you can contribute. You may make:

                  Pre-tax contributions
                  Roth contributions
                  Age 50 pre-tax and Roth catch-up contributions
                  After-tax contributions
                  Rollover contributions

                 You can change your contribution percentage at any time. Changes generally take 1-2 pay
                 periods to take effect.

                 For details, see "Plan Contributions" on page 9.

Vesting          You are always 100% vested in your account balance(s).

Investing Your   You choose how to invest your account from a variety of investment funds. If you do not
Account          make an investment election, your contributions will be invested in the BlackRock Life Path
                 Fund with the date closest to your 65th birthday.

                 For details, see "Investing Your Account" on page 13.

Withdrawals      You may be eligible to withdraw money from your account(s) while you are still working
                 with TPMG. The funds available to you will be based on your age and the reason you want
                 to make a withdrawal.

                 For details, see "Withdrawals and Loans" on page 14.

Taking a Loan    You may borrow from your account and repay the funds with interest.

                 The minimum loan amount is $1,000, and the maximum is the lesser of:

                       $50,000, less the amount of any other outstanding loans from the plan and all other
                           qualified plans maintained by TPMG or Mid-Atlantic Permanente Medical Group,
                           P.C. ("MAPMG") during the 12-month period prior to the new loan, or

                       half of your account balance.

Distribution of  You may not have more than two outstanding loans at a time, including and not limited to
Your Account     loans you may have taken from The Permanente Contribution Plan ("Plan 2").

Death Benefits   In general, all loans must be repaid within five years. However, you have up to 15 years to
                 repay loans taken to purchase your primary residence.

                 For details, see "Loans" on page 15.

                 You can receive your benefits when you retire, terminate your employment with TPMG and
                 MAPMG, or stop working because you become disabled. You may also defer payment until
                 a later date. Several forms of payment are available for you to choose from.

                 For details, see "Distribution of Your Account" on page 16.

                 If you die before your plan distribution begins, your beneficiary may be eligible to receive
                 benefits.

Eligibility and Enrollment

This section describes who is eligible for participation in the plan and when participation begins and ends. It also
includes important information on designating a beneficiary to receive any survivor benefits that may be payable in
the event of your death.

Eligibility for Plan 3 Membership

You are eligible for Plan 3 membership if you are a TPMG physician or salaried employee.
A physician is any employee of TPMG (including Pool physicians) who is paid under TPMG's physician payroll and:
 has a Doctor of Medicine or Doctor of Osteopathy degree,
 is a podiatrist,
 is an oral and maxillofacial surgeon, or
 is a TPMG Corporate officer as provided in the Plan.

A salaried employee is any employee of TPMG who:
 is paid on a salaried basis, or
 is a non-union, nonexempt employee.

You are not eligible if you:
 are not a TPMG physician or salaried employee,
 are covered by a collective bargaining agreement, unless the agreement specifically provides for participation

     in this plan, or
 participate in another qualified retirement plan or individual retirement account or annuity that TPMG contributes

     to, other than the Retirement Plan for Physicians and Salaried Employees of The Permanente Medical Group,
     Inc. ("Plan 1") or The Permanente Contribution Plan of the Permanente Medical Group, Inc. ("Plan 2").

5                Benefits Effective December 31, 2021
When Membership Begins

If you are eligible, your membership begins the first day of the month after you are hired by TPMG. You may elect
to begin contributions at that time. If you do not make an election, you will be automatically enrolled 30 days after
you become eligible. See "Automatic Enrollment" on page 6 and "How to Enroll" on page 6 for more information.

You will receive materials from the Fidelity Institutional Retirement Service Company (Fidelity), the plan's
recordkeeper, when you first become eligible. These materials will include information about how to enroll,
automatic enrollment, the different types of contributions, the investment options, how to make your investment
choices, and how to change your contribution level.

Automatic Enrollment

If you do not enroll when you first become eligible, you will be enrolled automatically in Plan 3 after 30 days. Your
contribution percentage will be 6% of your compensation, contributed as pre-tax elective deferrals. Contributions
will begin as of the first pay period after you are automatically enrolled.

Your contribution percentage will increase each year by 1% on each anniversary of the date contributions began,
until you reach a savings rate of 15%.

If you do not make an investment election before your automatic contributions begin, your contributions will be
invested in the BlackRock LifePath Fund with the date closest to your 65th birthday. You may change your
investment elections at any time.

If You Do Not Want to Contribute

You may choose not to contribute to the plan. In this case, you will need to elect that you do not want to contribute
and opt out of automatic enrollment. If you do not do this before contributions begin, you may elect to withdraw your
automatic savings, provided you do so within 90 days after of your automatic enrollment. For example, if you
were automatically enrolled on April 1, you will need to contact the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service
Center by June 30 to request a refund.

The refunded contribution plus any related earnings or losses will be paid to you as a lump sum. The refund will not
be considered an eligible rollover distribution and will not be subject to a 10% early withdrawal penalty. If you decide
at a later date to participate in the plan, you can enroll at any time. To request a refund, contact the TPMG
Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015 as soon as possible.

 Definition of "Compensation"

 Your Plan 3 compensation is your base pay, plus overtime pay, bonuses, and benefits paid in lieu of group health
 coverage, paid during the contribution period. Your compensation is not reduced by any salary deferrals you
 make to Plan 3 or any other pre-tax deferrals you make or contributions to a nonqualified deferred compensation
 plan.

How to Enroll

If you want to start contributions before the contributions from automatic enrollment begin or if you want to contribute
at a different percentage, you may actively enroll in the plan.

To enroll, contact the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015 or log on to Fidelity's
website at www.netbenefits.com/TPMG. You will be provided with the information and materials you need to enroll.

Benefits Effective December 31, 2021  6
Designating a Beneficiary

When you become a member of the plan, you should name a beneficiary or beneficiaries to receive any plan benefits
that may be payable in case of your death. To name a beneficiary, you need to complete the appropriate plan
beneficiary designation form and return it to MD Benefits.

Beneficiary designation forms can be found on www.netbenefits.com/TPMG. Return your completed beneficiary
designation form to MD Benefits by mail at 1800 Harrison Street, 7th Floor, Oakland, CA 94612, email at
MDBenefits@kp.org, or fax at 510-625-6260.

A beneficiary designation made by you must be received by MD Benefits prior to your death to be valid.

Important Facts about Beneficiary Designations

We encourage you review and/or update your beneficiary designation when you have a life event such as marriage,
divorce, or the birth or adoption of a child.

 If you name a beneficiary, they will remain your beneficiary until you either name a new beneficiary or marry (or
     remarry).

 If you marry, your spouse automatically becomes your beneficiary upon your marriage. You must have the
     consent of your spouse to name someone else as your beneficiary.

 Divorce does NOT automatically change your beneficiary if you have named a beneficiary by completing a valid
     beneficiary form.

 If you complete a beneficiary designation form naming your spouse as your beneficiary and you divorce your
     spouse (now former spouse), such former spouse will remain your beneficiary after the divorce until you either
     name a new beneficiary or remarry.

Non-Spouse Beneficiaries

If you are married and you want to name someone other than your spouse as your primary beneficiary, including
naming a trust or your estate, your spouse must provide written consent to your beneficiary designation. Your
spouse's consent must:

 be on a form provided by the plan,
 be witnessed by a Notary Public, and
 acknowledge an understanding of the effect of the consent.

If you marry after designating a non-spouse beneficiary, or if you divorce and remarry, your designation to your
non-spouse beneficiary (or to your former spouse) will no longer be valid. Your new spouse will automatically be
your beneficiary unless you elect otherwise.

 Definitions of "Married" and "Spouse"

 For all purposes of the plan, "married" means having a spouse and "spouse" means the person who is recognized
 as your spouse in accordance with laws of the State, the District of Columbia, a United States territory or a foreign
 jurisdiction. In accordance with applicable federal law, "spouse" does not include a domestic partner or a party
 to a civil union. Therefore, if you want your domestic partner or civil union partner to be your primary beneficiary,
 you must file a valid beneficiary designation form with MD Benefits.

7  Benefits Effective December 31, 2021
If You Die Without a Designated Beneficiary

If you die and MD Benefits does not have a valid beneficiary designation on file for you, any benefits will be payable
to the person or persons in the first of the following classes that survive you:
 spouse
 natural and adopted children and issue of deceased natural and adopted children by right of representation
 parents
 your estate
If you die without a valid beneficiary designation, your full account balance must be paid no later than December
31 following the fifth anniversary of your death.

 Is Your Beneficiary Designation Valid?

 Your beneficiary designation may be invalid for a number of reasons, such as:
  you do not name a beneficiary;
  the beneficiary you name does not survive you;
  the beneficiary designation filed is vague or ambiguous;
  the designated beneficiary cannot be reasonably identified; or
  the Plan Administrator does not receive a signed and dated beneficiary designation form before your death.
 You are encouraged to review your beneficiary designation(s) on file with MD Benefits periodically and update
 the beneficiary designation form as needed.
 To designate a beneficiary, you can request the appropriate plan beneficiary designation form from MD Benefits
 or download from Fidelity's website at www.netbenefits.com/TPMG. You must return the form to MD Benefits.

Death of Beneficiary Prior to Beneficiary's Account Distribution

If you die and your designated beneficiary dies before the beneficiary's account balance is fully distributed, the
remaining account balance will be paid to your beneficiary's estate.

When Membership Ends

Your membership in Plan 3 ends when the earliest of the following events occurs:
 you have received a total distribution of your account, or
 your death.

Benefits Effective December 31, 2021  8
Plan Contributions

As a Plan 3 member, there are several ways in which you may contribute to the plan, including:

 Pre-tax contributions,
 Roth contributions,
 Age 50 pre-tax and Roth catch-up contributions,
 After-tax contributions, and
 Rollover contributions.

All of your contributions are kept in separate accounts maintained under your name, based on the types of
contribution.

Changing Your Contributions

You may change your contribution levels and/or the type of future contribution at any time by contacting the TPMG
Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015 or log on to www.netbenefits.com/TPMG. Your
change will be effective as soon as administratively possible, generally 1-2 pay periods.

Contributions If You Are on Military Leave

If you go on active military leave while employed by TPMG and you are a member of the plan, you may be entitled
to make additional contributions to the plan if you are reinstated or reemployed by TPMG within the time frames
prescribed by the Uniformed Services Employment and Reemployment Rights Act of 1994 ("USERRA"). Your
contributions will be based on the compensation you would have received while you were on leave. If this amount
is not clear, your contribution will be based on your 12-month average compensation earned immediately before
your leave began. However, you cannot contribute more than the maximum amount that you would have been able
to contribute if you had been an active employee during your leave.

Pre-Tax Elective Deferral Contributions

You can contribute from 1% to 75% of your compensation on a pre-tax basis. You do not pay federal income taxes
on the money you contribute or the earnings on that money until you withdraw them from the plan. Please note that
your pre-tax savings are subject to Social Security (FICA) taxes.

The amount you can contribute is limited by the Internal Revenue Service. For 2021, the maximum contribution is
$19,500. This amount is subject to change from year to year and includes any Roth elective deferrals you may
make. Please see "Internal Revenue Service Limits" on page 12 for more information.

As described under "When Membership Begins" on page 6, after you first become eligible to participate, TPMG will
automatically enroll you in the plan at a 6% pre-tax contribution rate, unless you elect to contribute at a different
level or you opt out of contributing. This 6% pre-tax contribution rate will increase each year by 1% until your
contribution rate is 15% of your compensation, unless you elect a different amount or elect to cease contributions.

9  Benefits Effective December 31, 2021
Example of How Pre-Tax Elective Deferrals Can Save You Money

Saving through pre-tax elective deferrals can reduce your current taxes. Suppose you earn $6,000 per month. You
save 6% of your salary through pre-tax elective deferrals. For purposes of this example, we'll assume you pay 25%
of your salary in federal income tax. Following is an example of how saving on a pre-tax basis reduces your federal
income tax.

 The Advantage of Pre-tax Elective Deferrals

 When you save money on a pre-tax basis, in the year of deferral you do not pay income tax on the amount you
 defer. You will owe income tax when you withdraw the money from your account. Depending on where you live,
 you may also pay less in local and state taxes.

Example of Pre-Tax Savings  Without Pre-Tax Savings  With Pre-Tax Savings

Your Gross Monthly Pay                 $6,000         $6,000
Your 6% Savings                            - $0        - $360
Your Taxable Income                                   $5,640
Your Federal Taxes                     $6,000        - $1,410
Your Monthly Tax Savings              - $1,500
Annual Tax Savings                                         $90
                                             $0       $1,080
                                             $0

Note that this example is for illustrative purposes only. Your actual tax rate depends on your individual
circumstances.

Roth Elective Deferrals

You can make Roth elective deferrals of 1% to 75% of your compensation. If you make pre-tax elective deferrals
as well as Roth elective deferrals, the combined total of your contributions cannot be more than 75% of your
compensation.

With Roth elective deferrals, you pay taxes prior to making the contribution, but you do not pay taxes on the money
when it is withdrawn. Taxes on any investment earnings will be deferred until you withdraw the money. However,
withdrawals of investment earnings are not taxed if:

 you have had your Roth elective deferral account for at least five years, and
 you are at least age 59 ˝ or disabled, or you have died.

If you withdraw money before age 59 ˝, you will pay a 10% penalty on the amount of the distribution.

As with the pre-tax elective deferrals, the amount of your Roth elective deferrals is limited by the Internal Revenue
Service. For 2021, the maximum contribution is $19,500. This amount is subject to change from year to year and
includes any pre-tax elective deferrals you may make.

Benefits Effective December 31, 2021                                       10
Roth Conversions

You may convert all or a portion of your pre-tax and/or after-tax contributions to Roth 401(k) contributions at any
time. For future contributions, the Plan offers an automatic in-plan Roth conversion feature that allows your after-
tax contributions to be converted to Roth immediately after each contribution is made. These amounts will remain
in the Plan and do not need to be rolled over into a Roth IRA.

To start using the automatic in-plan Roth conversion feature or to request a one-time in-plan Roth conversion,
please contact the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015.

Pre-tax amounts that are converted to Roth amounts will be subject to taxation in the year the conversion is made.

 If you take a distribution of converted amounts after those amounts have been in the Roth account for at least
     five years and you are at least age 59 ˝ or more at the time of the distribution, the entire amount, including
     earnings, will be tax-free.

 If you take a distribution of converted amounts from your Roth Account prior to attaining age 59 ˝ and/or within
     five years of their conversion, all or part of your distribution may be subject to income tax or penalties. You are
     encouraged to consult with a financial advisor regarding potential tax implications prior to requesting a
     distribution.

Catch-up Contributions

If you are age 50 or older by the end of any calendar year, you may make a separate "catch-up" contribution of 1%
up to 75% each year in addition to your pre-tax elective deferrals and/or your Roth elective deferrals.

The maximum combined catch-up contribution you may make for 2021 is $6,500. If you are eligible to make a catch-
up contribution, you can contribute as much as $26,000 in 2021 as pre-tax elective deferrals or Roth elective
deferrals or a combination of both. This amount is subject to change from year to year. Please see "Internal Revenue
Service Limits" on page 12 for more information.

You may elect to make catch-up contributions at any time after you are enrolled in the plan and meet the eligibility
requirements above.

After-Tax Contributions

You may make contributions on an after-tax basis of up to 25% of your compensation, but not more than the
maximum allowed under the Plan and applicable tax laws that limit the total combined amount that can be
contributed to this Plan and Plan 2. The maximum after-tax contribution for 2021 is $16,640, but in some limited
circumstances may be lower under law laws and is subject to change at any time. After-tax contributions can only
be made through payroll deduction.

Your contributions (payroll deductions) will generally stop once the maximum allowable contributions amount is
reached. However, if your after-tax contributions for any Plan Year exceed the limit, the excess will be distributed
to you by the end of the following year.

Your election will go into effect as soon as administratively practicable, generally 1-2 pay periods, and continues
from year to year unless you make a change.

Rollover Contributions

The plan accepts rollovers of some distributions from certain retirement plans. By making a rollover contribution,
you defer paying taxes on the distributions that you are rolling over. You may roll over an eligible distribution from:

 the Retirement Plan for Physicians and Salaried Employees of The Permanente Medical Group, Inc. ("Plan
     1") (direct rollover only);

 another employer's qualified retirement plan that meets the requirements of Section 401(a), 401(k), 403(a), or
     403(b) of the Internal Revenue Code;

 an individual retirement account or annuity other than a Roth IRA;

11  Benefits Effective December 31, 2021
 a government 457(b) plan;
 a Roth elective deferral account under another retirement plan (direct rollover only).

The minimum rollover amount is $1,000.

You may make a direct rollover, direct transfer of the distribution into the plan, or an indirect rollover, the distribution
is paid to you and you put the funds in the plan within 60 days of receipt. (However, an indirect rollover may be
subject to taxation on some of the funds that you have received.)

To make a rollover, call the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015. The service
center will provide you the necessary forms and ensure that your rollover meets any eligibility requirements. You
can also log on to www.netbenefits.com/TPMG and download rollover forms. Completed forms must be returned to
Fidelity.

Internal Revenue Service Limits

Internal Revenue Service rules impose certain limits on contributions to the plan and the compensation that may
be taken into account. All limits are subject to change from year to year, and other limits may be imposed. You will
be notified if you are affected by any of these.

Contributions to another employer's retirement plans may limit the total contributions the IRS allows you to
contribute under the plan. If you participated in another employer's retirement plan during the year, please consult
with your tax advisor and notify TPMG if your contributions to the plans exceed an applicable IRS limit.

The amount you can contribute as pre-tax elective deferrals and/or Roth elective deferrals each year is limited by
the IRS. The IRS combined maximum for all plans for 2021 is $19,500. If you are eligible to make catch-up
contributions, the 2021 limit is increased by $6,500 for combined maximum of $26,000.

The IRS also limits the total combined amount of all contributions (including pre-tax, Roth, after-tax, and employer
contributions) that can be contributed each year by you and your employer(s). The IRS combined maximum for all
plans for 2021 is $58,000 ($64,500 if you are eligible for catch-up contributions). This limit applies to total
contributions a member and TPMG may make each year to this plan and any other TPMG and MAPMG plan in
which the member participates, including Plan 2.

The annual compensation that can be taken into account for plan purposes is $290,000 for 2021.

IRS regulations also require that the plan pass a nondiscrimination, or fairness, test designed to ensure an equitable
level of contributions by employees at different pay levels. To satisfy the test, the contributions of some highly
compensated employees (as defined by the Internal Revenue Service) may have to be further limited. Generally,
this will affect TPMG's top-paid 20% for the prior plan year.

Vesting

Being vested means that you have a non-forfeitable right to your account balance(s).

You are always 100% vested in your account balance(s).

Benefits Effective December 31, 2021  12
