Initial Investments

When you become a plan member, you will receive information on your investment options from Fidelity. To make
your initial investments, contact the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015, or log
on to Fidelity's website at www.netbenefits.com/TPMG. You will need to establish login credentials and a password
for future transactions.

If you do not make an investment election, your contributions will be invested in the BlackRock LifePath Fund with
the date closest to your 65th birthday, which is the qualified default investment alternative designated by the TPMG
Retirement Program Committee.

Changing Your Investments

You may change your investment mix or transfer your investments between funds at any time. Call the TPMG
Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015, or log on to www.netbenefits.com/TPMG. If your
transaction is confirmed before 1 p.m. Pacific time, it will take place on the same day. If your transaction is confirmed
after 1 p.m. Pacific time, it will take place the next business day.

Keeping Track of Your Accounts

You can call the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015 or log on to
www.netbenefits.com/TPMG generally at any time for information about your account, including your account
balances. You may also make transactions such as:

· changing contribution amounts
· changing investment elections

13                                                             Benefits Effective December 31, 2021
 requesting information about the investment fund options
 requesting a withdrawal
 applying for a loan
 requesting a distribution

Withdrawals and Loans

If you need to access the money in your accounts while you are still working, you may make a withdrawal or borrow
from your account.

Withdrawals

There are three types of withdrawals:

 After-tax contribution withdrawals
 Age 59 ˝ withdrawals
 Hardship withdrawals

You may make one withdrawal per calendar quarter.

If you are married, your spouse must provide written notarized consent to receive the withdrawal. This consent must
be provided within 90 days before the withdrawal.

After-Tax Contribution Withdrawals

You may withdraw all or any portion of your voluntary after-tax employee contributions and any investment earnings
on these contributions, once per calendar quarter for any reason. You will not pay taxes on your contributions, but
you will pay taxes on any part of the withdrawal that is considered investment earnings. Please see "Taxes on
Distributions" on page 18 for more information.

Age 59 1/2 Withdrawals

Once you reach the age of 59 ˝, you may withdraw all or a portion of your contributions and any investment
earnings, once per calendar quarter for any reason, regardless of the type of contribution, even if you are still
working for TPMG, and there will be no 10% penalty tax for early distribution. Please see "Taxes on Distributions"
on page 18 for more information.

Hardship Withdrawals

You can withdraw your pre-tax elective contributions and your Roth elective contributions (and any investment
earnings on these contributions) if you have a financial hardship. You will be required to provide documentation to
show that you have a financial hardship.

You will have to pay applicable taxes on the money you withdraw from your pre-tax account, and in most cases an
additional 10% penalty tax. Please see "Taxes on Distributions" on page 18 for more information.

Financial hardship means you have an immediate and heavy financial need, and you have no other funds readily
available to meet that need. Hardship withdrawals are available only in specific circumstances. The following
expenses constitute a need as hardship withdrawals:

 certain medical expenses deductible under IRC Sec. 213
 costs related to the purchase of a principal residence (excluding mortgage payments)
 payment of tuition, room and board, and related educational fees for the next 12 months of post-secondary

     education for you, your spouse, or dependents as defined by IRC Sec. 152
 payments necessary to prevent eviction or mortgage foreclosure on your principal residence
 payments for burial or funeral expenses for your deceased parent, spouse, children, or dependents
 expenses relating to repairs of damage to your principal residence that would qualify for the IRC Sec. 165

     casualty deduction

Benefits Effective December 31, 2021                       14
 expenses and losses (including loss of income) incurred by you on account of a disaster declared by the
     Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) provided that your principal residence or place of
     employment is located in a disaster area

 other expenses that TPMG determines constitute an immediate and heavy need within IRS rules

If you take a hardship withdrawal, the funds will be withdrawn in the following order:

 Pre-tax elective deferrals
 Pre-tax elective deferral catch-up contributions
 Rollover contributions
 Roth elective deferrals
 Roth elective deferral catch-up contributions
 Roth conversion contributions

Applying for a Hardship Withdrawal

To apply for hardship withdrawal, contact the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-
4015 or log on to Fidelity's website at www.netbenefits.com/TPMG. You will be provided with detailed information
on how to request a hardship withdrawal. Send your completed hardship withdrawal forms and documentation to
Fidelity.

If you are married, your spouse must provide written notarized consent to the hardship withdrawal. This consent
must be provided within 90 days before the hardship withdrawal.

Loans

You may borrow from your account and repay the funds with interest.

The minimum loan amount is $1,000, and the maximum is the lesser of:

      $50,000, less the amount of any other outstanding loans from the plan and all other qualified plans
          maintained by TPMG or MAPMG during the 12-month period prior to the new loan, or

      half of your account balance in the plan.

You may not have more than two outstanding loans at a time, including loans you may have taken from Plan 2.

The interest rate on the loan will be based on the prime interest rate plus one percent.

Loans are funded proportionately based on assets from all your investment funds except from the self-directed
brokerage account (Fidelity BrokerageLink).

All loans must be repaid within five years, although loans to purchase a home that will be your principal residence
may be repaid over a maximum period of 15 years.

Applying for a Loan

To apply for a loan, contact the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service Center at 1-800-889-4015. You will
be provided with detailed information about plan loans, including current interest rates, any costs relating to taking
out a loan, and the terms for repayment. You can also log on to www.netbenefits.com/TPMG to download loan
forms. Send your completed loan forms to Fidelity.

If you are married, your spouse must provide written notarized consent to the loan. This consent must be provided
within 90 days before the loan goes into effect.

Repaying Your Loan

In general, loans will be repaid through payroll deductions. Repayments will be made directly to the account from
which the funds were borrowed and will be invested according to your current investment elections.

If you stop working with TPMG, or if you become disabled or die, before your loan is repaid, your account will be
reduced by the amount of the outstanding loan unless you agree to a repayment schedule. The outstanding loan

15  Benefits Effective December 31, 2021
balance, including interest, will be considered a distribution from the plan and subject to the appropriate income
taxes. You may choose, however, to repay the loan balance in full, instead of having it treated as a distribution.

If you do not repay your loan as scheduled, you will be considered in default, and you will be prohibited from taking
another loan from Plan 2 and Plan 3 until after a period of time equal to the term of the defaulted loan.

If you are on military leave, you do not have to repay your loan until you return to active employment with TPMG.

Distribution of Your Account

You may take a distribution from the plan when you reach age 59 ˝, retire, become disabled (as defined by the
plan), or terminate employment from TPMG and MAPMG.

Distributions are funded proportionately based on assets from all your investment funds except from the self-
directed brokerage account (Fidelity BrokerageLink).

You have the choice of several payment forms, including:

           lump sum
           partial distributions
           periodic installments over a period of time not to exceed your life expectancy, as elected by you, and

                paid at least once a year
           single life annuity (if you are not married)
           qualified joint and 100% survivor annuity or a 50% or 66-2/3% joint and survivor annuity (if you are

                married)

Please note if you are married, your spouse must provide written, notarized consent to any form of payment other
than the qualified joint and survivor annuity with your spouse as beneficiary.

If your account balance is $1,000 or less, it will automatically be paid in one lump sum, regardless of your marital
status.

Your plan distribution(s) are taxable. See the section called "Taxes on Distributions" on page 18 for more
information.

Lump Sum

With the lump sum payment option, you receive your entire account balance in one payment. No further benefit is
then payable.

Partial Distributions

With the partial distribution payment option, you receive partial withdrawals (up to one per calendar quarter) before
you begin to receive another optional form of payment described in this section.

Periodic Installments

With the periodic installments payment option, you receive installment payments made at least once per year. Once
payments begin, you may elect to receive one additional payment each calendar quarter.

Annuities

With the annuity payment options, your entire account balance will be used to purchase an annuity that pays monthly
benefit payments to you for your lifetime and, if you are married, pays the same or a reduced monthly benefit for
your spouse's lifetime.

If you are not married, your annuity option is a single life annuity, which is a monthly payment for your lifetime only
with no survivor benefit. Unmarried members are not eligible for joint and survivor annuity options.

If you are married, you may choose a 50%, 66-2/3% or 100% joint and survivor annuity option. With these options,
your account balance is used to purchase an annuity that pays you a monthly benefit for your lifetime, with 50%,

Benefits Effective December 31, 2021  16
66-2/3%, or 100% of that amount continuing to your surviving spouse for their lifetime. Married members are not
eligible for the single life annuity option.

Election Period

Any election regarding the time and form of payment of your retirement benefits must be made during your election
period, which is the 90-day period before your benefits begin, and must be made in the form and manner designated
by the Plan Administrator. You may revoke your election at any time before you start receiving benefits.

Benefits If You Die

Upon your death, your account balance will be payable to your beneficiary. See "Designating a Beneficiary" on page
7 for more information.

Your beneficiary may elect one of the following payment methods.

      Lump Sum: Your beneficiary receives your entire account balance in one payment. No further benefit is
          payable.

      Installments: Your beneficiary receives installment payments made at least once per year, not to exceed
          their life expectancy. Once payments begin, your beneficiary may elect to receive one additional payment
          each calendar quarter.

      Qualified Pre-retirement Survivor Annuity: Your full account balance is used to purchase an annuity that
          provides monthly payments to your spouse for their lifetime.

          You may waive this benefit with your spouse's written consent. If you waive this benefit before age 35, your
          waiver will expire when you reach age 35 and you will need to complete a new waiver with your spouse's
          written consent.

          If you are married and your spouse is your beneficiary, the payment method will be the Qualified Pre-
          retirement Survivor Annuity, unless you waived this payment form or your spouse elects another payment
          form.

Your beneficiary may be eligible to roll over your account balance to another plan or IRA. See "Direct Rollover"
below for more information about rollovers.

In the event of the subsequent death of your beneficiary, any unpaid account balance will be paid to the estate of
your beneficiary.

Direct Rollover

You (or your spousal beneficiary) may roll over a plan distribution into another employer's qualified retirement plan,
403(b) plan or governmental 457(b) plan that accepts rollovers, or into an individual retirement account or annuity
("IRA"), including a Roth IRA. The rollover must be a direct rollover, meaning the distribution is made directly from
this plan to the trustee or custodian of the other plan or IRA. A designated beneficiary other than your spouse may
roll over a plan distribution into an inherited IRA.

Certain types of payments are not eligible for rollover. You can roll over lump sum distributions and partial
distributions. You cannot roll over periodic distributions, such as installment payments or annuity payments, or
required minimum distributions.

The minimum direct rollover amount is $500. When you receive a distribution, you will receive more detailed
information about tax consequences and the rollover rules.

17  Benefits Effective December 31, 2021
Required Minimum Distribution

Based on federal tax law, required minimum distributions (RMDs) must be made under the plan by the beginning
dates listed below. RMDs are the minimum distribution amounts you must withdraw from your account each year.
Once you reach age 72, you must begin receiving distributions by April 1 of the following year or after the year in
which you retire, if you are still working (unless you reached age 70˝ prior to January 1, 2020).
If you are at least age 72 and still employed by TPMG or MAPMG, you may defer distribution until you retire from
TPMG and MAPMG. However, you may elect to receive a full or partial distribution of your account balance at any
time before you leave TPMG or MAPMG. Consult with your tax advisor regarding the tax implications of receiving
or deferring distributions while you continue to work for TPMG or MAPMG.

 Deferring Benefits

 You can defer benefits, but payment must begin by your Required Beginning Date.
 Your Required Beginning Date is the later of April 1 of the first calendar year following the later of:

             the year in which you reach age 72 (unless you reached age 70˝ prior to January 1, 2020); or
             the year in which you no longer work for TPMG and MAPMG.

Taxes on Distributions

Upon receiving a distribution, you or your beneficiary will be responsible for paying ordinary income tax on the
taxable portion of your account. Roth elective deferrals, Roth conversions, and voluntary after-tax employee
contributions will not be taxed because they were already taxed before they went into your account. Generally, pre-
tax elective deferrals, rollover contributions, and all investments earnings are taxable upon distribution. Special
rules apply to Roth earnings.

If a distribution is made before age 59 ˝ for any reason other than your death, disability, or retirement on or after
age 55, the taxable portion of this distribution will be subject to a nondeductible 10% excise tax in addition to ordinary
income tax. Upon receiving a distribution, you or your beneficiary will be responsible for paying ordinary income tax
on the taxable portion of the distribution.

Current regulations require that the plan withhold for federal taxes, 20% of the taxable amount of any distribution
(other than a hardship withdrawal) that is not rolled over.

You can defer the payment of income taxes and avoid the 20% withholding and any applicable tax penalty by
instructing Fidelity to roll over the eligible balance directly into an individual retirement account (IRA), including a
Roth IRA, or another eligible retirement plan, including a 403(b) tax-sheltered annuity or a governmental 457(b)
plan.

Another option is for you to receive your account balance and then roll it over yourself into another qualified plan or
IRA within 60 days from the date of receipt. In this case, you defer income taxes, but the 20% withholding is still
deducted from the plan payment. As a result, only 80% of your account balance is available to be rolled over, and
the remaining 20% would be taxable. To roll over an amount equal to 100% of your account balance and defer
taxes on the full amount of your account balance, you will need to use other money to replace the 20% that was
withheld for taxes.

Any taxable amount you roll over into a Roth IRA will be includible in your taxable income at the time it is paid from
the plan; however, mandatory withholding does not apply. If certain conditions are met, withdrawals from a Roth
IRA, unlike a regular IRA, may be tax-free.

Tax laws are complicated and change often. TPMG cannot provide tax advice. You are encouraged to consult a
tax advisor to discuss how these rules apply to your individual situation. Should you (or your surviving spouse or
other beneficiary) become eligible to receive a lump-sum distribution from the plan, more detailed information will
be provided at that time.

Benefits Effective December 31, 2021  18
Applying for Benefits

To request a distribution of benefits from your plan account, call the TPMG Retirement and Savings Plans Service
Center at 1-800-889-4015 or log on to www.netbenefits.com/TPMG.

Fidelity can provide you or your beneficiary with the necessary benefit application, election and tax forms, and guide
you through the application process. You must complete all required forms and file them with Fidelity before any
benefits can be paid to you. Application forms are not considered filed until they are received by Fidelity.

A claim for benefits must be made in writing within 360 days after payment of the claimed benefit is due.

Denied Claims

If your application or other claim for benefits is denied, in whole or in part, the TPMG Benefits Manager (or designee)
will notify you in writing or electronically of the denial within a reasonable period of time of no more than 90 days
after the plan receives your claim.

If due to special circumstances additional time is required to consider and respond to your claim, you will be notified
in writing before the expiration of the initial 90-day period and the time for responding to your claim may be extended
by up to an additional 90 days. The notice will describe the special circumstances requiring the extension, including
whether additional information is required to decide your claim, and the date by which the TPMG Benefits Manager
(or designee) expects to make a determination.

If your claim concerns your disability and the claim is denied, the notice of denial described above will be provided
within 45 days (not 90 days) and if special circumstances require an extension of time to respond to your claim, the
extension will be no more than 30 days. The TPMG Benefits Manager may further extend this period for up to an
additional 30 days by notifying you in writing before the end of the first 30-day extension.

A notice of claim denial will:

      State the specific reasons why the claim is denied;
      Identify the specific plan provisions on which the denial is based;
      Describe any additional material or information that is required before the claim can be approved, and why

          that information is needed;
      Explain the steps that you need to take (and the applicable time limits) to appeal the denial of your claim

          and your right to bring civil action under section 502(a) of ERISA if you file an appeal and your appeal is
          denied;
      State the time limits described below for initiating any legal action involving a benefit claim.

This notice will include additional information if your claim concerns your disability and is denied in whole or in part
based on a finding that you are not disabled, including (a) a discussion of the decision including the basis for
disagreeing with the views of any healthcare, medical or vocational professionals who evaluated you or whose
advice was obtained in connection with your appeal, (b) a statement that information concerning scientific or clinical
judgments relating to the decision will be provided upon request, (c) any rules, guidelines, protocols, standards or
similar criteria relied upon in making the determination or a statement that none exist, (d) a statement that you are
entitled to receive, upon request and free of charge, reasonable access to and copies of all documents, records
and other information relevant to your claim. The notice will be provided in a culturally and linguistically appropriate
manner. Details concerning such additional information are set out in Section 8.3 of the plan document which is
available upon request.

You may consider your claim denied and proceed to the appeal stage described below if the TPMG Benefits
Manager (or designee) does not respond to your claim within 90 days (45 days if your claim is for disability benefits).
If you do not file a timely appeal, the TPMG Benefits Manager's (or designee's) decision will be final,
binding, and conclusive on all concerned and you will not have the right to bring a civil action under section
502(a) of ERISA.

19  Benefits Effective December 31, 2021
Review of Denied Claims/Filing an Appeal

If your claim is denied in whole or in part, you may appeal the denial. To appeal a denied claim, you, your beneficiary,
or your authorized representative must file a written appeal with:

          Administrative Committee
          c/o MD Benefits
          1800 Harrison Street, 7th Floor
          Oakland, CA 94612

You must file your appeal within 60 days (180 days if your claim is for disability benefits) of the date you received
the denial notice. You should explain the basis for your appeal and submit any relevant written comments,
documents, records, or other information.

You will be provided, upon request and free of charge, reasonable access to, and copies of, all documents, records,
and other information relevant to your request for appeal.

A document, record, or other information is considered relevant to the claim if it:

      was relied on in making the benefit decision,
      was submitted, considered, or generated in the course of making the benefit decision (without regard to

          whether it was relied on in making the decision), or
      demonstrates compliance with the requirement that benefit decisions follow the terms of the plan and be

          consistently applied to similarly situated claimants.

Appeal Process

The Administrative Committee or its designee will decide your appeal within a reasonable period of time, but no
later than 60 days (45 days if your claim is for disability benefits) after it receives your appeal. However, the
Administrative Committee (or designee) may need more time -- up to 120 days (90 days if your claim is for disability
benefits) after it receives your appeal -- to make a decision due to special circumstances. If an extension of time
is required because of special circumstances, you will be given written notice of the extension before the expiration
of the initial determination period. The written extension notice will indicate the special circumstances requiring the
extension and the date by which the committee expects to render a decision.

The Administrative Committee will consider all comments, documents, records, and other information that you have
submitted in reviewing your claim, regardless of whether that information was considered in determining your initial
claim.

If your claim is for disability benefits, the review will not defer to the original denial and will be decided by the
Administrative Committee. If your claim was denied based on medical judgment, the Administrative Committee will
consult with a health care professional, who has training and experience in the particular medical field involved, and
who is different from the person, or their subordinate, who was consulted in connection with the denial of your initial
claim.

The Administrative Committee will also identify any medical or vocational expert whose advice was obtained in
connection with the denial of your initial claim (without regard to whether the advice was relied upon in denying your
claim) upon request. The Administrative Committee (or designee) will provide you, free of charge, with any new or
additional evidence generated, considered or relied upon in deciding your appeal, and any new or additional
rationale on which its decision may be based. This information will be provided to you as soon as possible so that
you have time to respond before the Administrative Committee must decide your appeal.

Denied Appeals

If your appeal is denied in whole or in part, the Administrative Committee (or designee) will notify you in writing or
electronically within a reasonable period of time. This notice of the denial of your appeal will include:

      the specific reasons for the denial;
      the specific plan provisions on which the denial is based;

Benefits Effective December 31, 2021  20
      a statement that you are entitled to receive, upon request and free of charge, reasonable access to, and
          copies of, all documents, records, and other information relevant to your claim (a document is considered
          relevant if it meets one or more of the criteria listed at the end of the "Review of Denied Claims/Filing an
          Appeal" section, under "Denied Claims" on page 20);

      a statement of your right to bring a civil action under ERISA section 502(a) following a denial of your appeal;
      the time limits described below for initiating any legal action involving a benefit claim.

If your appeal concerns your disability and is denied in whole or in part based on a finding that you are not disabled,
this notice will also include: (a) a discussion of the decision including the basis for disagreeing with the views of any
healthcare, medical or vocational professionals who evaluated you or whose advice was obtained in connection
with your appeal, (b) a statement that information concerning scientific or clinical judgments relating to the decision
will be provided upon request, (c) any rules, guidelines, protocols, standards or similar criteria relied upon in making
the determination or a statement that none exist. The notice will be provided in a culturally and linguistically
appropriate manner. Details concerning such additional information are set out in Section 8.3 of the plan document
which is available upon request.

If you do not receive notice of the denial of your appeal within the time allowed, you may consider your appeal
denied. Decisions by the Administrative Committee are final, binding, and conclusive on all concerned and
shall be given the maximum possible deference allowed by law.

The Administrative Committee has discretionary authority to make findings of fact and to interpret and apply the
terms of the plan in connection with claims and appeals.

You may not initiate a lawsuit to obtain plan benefits until after you have exhausted the claims and appeals
procedures described above. No lawsuit may be initiated more than 360 days after the claims and appeals
procedures described above have been exhausted. Any lawsuit concerning the Plan must be brought in the United
States District Court for the Northern District of California.

The specific procedures governing claims for medical benefits (including, but not limited to, procedures for urgent
care claims, concurrent care decisions, pre-service and post-service claims, procedures for filing claim forms,
providing notifications of benefit determinations, and reviewing denied claims) applicable to the medical plans
sponsored by TPMG are provided to you automatically, and free of charge, as a separate document.

Other Rules and Regulations

This section describes additional rules and regulations that may affect your benefits, as well as your rights under
laws such as the Employee Retirement Income Security Act of 1974 (as amended), known as "ERISA."

Benefits Not Insured

The Pension Benefit Guaranty Corporation ("PBGC"), a federal insurance agency, insures certain types of benefits
under defined benefit plans. Because Plan 3 is a defined contribution plan and your benefits are based on your
Plan 3 account balance(s), benefits are not insured by the PBGC.

Qualified Domestic Relations Order ("QDRO")

Generally, your benefits under the plan cannot be assigned, either voluntarily or involuntarily, except through a
qualified domestic relations order or "QDRO."
In the event of your divorce or another domestic relations matter, a QDRO may legally require the distribution of a
portion of your plan benefit to an alternate payee (your spouse, former spouse, child, or other dependent). Your
alternate payee may elect to receive an immediate distribution from the newly established account following the
qualification of the QDRO.
Your benefit will be reduced if a court has ordered that a portion of your total accrued benefit is to be paid to an
alternate payee under a QDRO.

21  Benefits Effective December 31, 2021
You may obtain a free copy of the plan's QDRO procedures from the QDRO administrator by contacting QDRO
Consultants at 1-800-527-8481. You will also be provided with information describing your rights, plan benefits, and
how the determination process works.
If you have a pending domestic relations order, you may not begin to receive any distribution from the plan. If a
distribution has already started, a portion of the distribution may be withheld pending resolution of the QDRO review
process.

Potential Loss of Benefits

The plan is intended to provide you with a valuable retirement benefit. However, some individuals may not qualify
for a benefit and others may lose a benefit even if they once qualified. Circumstances resulting in a denial or loss
of benefits are discussed more fully elsewhere in this SPD. You should be aware that the following are some, but
not all, of the possible reasons you may not receive part or all of a benefit:
 If you do not meet the requirements for eligibility to participate, you will not be entitled to any benefit.
 If all or a portion of your benefits are awarded to an alternate payee pursuant to a QDRO, you will not receive

     your entire benefit.
 If the plan should be disqualified by the IRS, contributions made to the plan may result in current taxable

     income to you.
 If the investments you select decrease in value.

Your ERISA Rights

As a member of the plan, you are entitled to certain rights and protections under the Employee Retirement Income
Security Act of 1974 ("ERISA"). ERISA provides that all plan participants shall have the following rights.

Receive Information about Your Plan and Benefits

ERISA provides that all plan participants shall be entitled to:

 Examine without charge, at the plan administrator's office, all documents governing the plan, including
     insurance contracts, collective bargaining agreements, and a copy of the latest annual report (Form 5500
     Series) filed by the plan with the U.S. Department of Labor and available at the Public Disclosure Room of the
     Employee Benefits Security Administration.

 Obtain, upon written request to the plan administrator, copies of documents governing the operation of the
     plan, including insurance contracts, collective bargaining agreements, and copies of the latest annual report
     (Form 5500 Series) and updated summary plan description. The plan administrator may make a reasonable
     charge for the copies.

 Receive a summary of the plan's annual financial report. The plan administrator is required by law to furnish
     each plan member with a copy of this summary annual report.

23  Benefits Effective December 31, 2021
 Obtain a statement telling you whether you have a right to receive a pension at normal retirement age, and if
     so, what your benefits would be at normal retirement age if you stop working under the plan now. If you do not
     have a right to a pension, the statement will tell you how many more years you have to work to get a right to a
     pension. This statement must be requested in writing and is not required to be given more than once every 12
     months. The plan must provide the statement free of charge.

Prudent Actions by Plan Fiduciaries

In addition to creating rights for plan members, ERISA imposes duties upon the people who are responsible for the
operation of the plan. The people who operate your plan, called "fiduciaries" of the plan, have a duty to do so
prudently and in the interest of you, other plan members, and beneficiaries.

No one, including your employer or any other person, may fire you or otherwise discriminate against you in any way
to prevent you from obtaining a pension or welfare benefit or exercising your rights under ERISA.

Enforce Your Rights

If your claim for a benefit is denied or ignored, in whole or in part, you have a right to know why this was done, to
obtain copies of documents relating to the decision without charge, and to appeal any denial, all within certain time
schedules.

Under ERISA, there are steps you can take to enforce the above rights. For instance, if you request a copy of plan
documents or the latest annual report from the plan and do not receive them within 30 days, you may file suit in a
federal court. In such a case, the court may require the plan administrator to provide the materials and pay you up
to $110 a day until you receive the materials, unless the materials were not sent because of reasons beyond the
control of the plan administrator.

If you have a claim for benefits that is denied or ignored, in whole or in part, you may file suit in a state or federal
court. In addition, if you disagree with the plan's decision or lack thereof concerning the qualified status of a domestic
relations order, you may file suit in federal court. If it should happen that plan fiduciaries misuse the plan's money,
or if you are discriminated against for asserting your rights, you may seek assistance from the U.S. Department of
Labor, or you may file suit in a federal court. The court will decide who should pay costs and legal fees. If you are
successful, the court may order the person you have sued to pay these costs and fees. If you lose, the court may
order you to pay the costs and fees, if for example, it finds your claim is frivolous.

Assistance with Your Questions

If you have any questions about your plan, you should contact the plan administrator. If you have any questions
about this statement or about your rights under ERISA, or if you need assistance in obtaining documents from the
plan administrator, you should contact the nearest Office of the Employee Benefits Security Administration, U.S.
Department of Labor, listed in your telephone directory or the Division of Technical Assistance and Inquiries,
Employee Benefits Security Administration, U.S. Department of Labor, 200 Constitution Avenue N.W., Washington,
D.C. 20210. You may also obtain certain publications about your rights and responsibilities under ERISA by calling
the publications hotline of the Employee Benefits Security Administration.
